"Chapter XXXII."
"Of the treatment of prominent teeth compared to others."
When teeth protrude beyond their natural course due to form being distorted, especially in women and venerable elders; therefore you should consider: if the tooth is not adjacent to another tooth, and there is no possibility of extraction or splinting, then it must be removed. But if it is attached to another tooth, then you should cut it with this instrument whose shape resembles a pig's bristle made from Indian steel with an extremely sharp tip.
And may your incision be such that you cut through the tooth in three days due to its hardness, without harming any other teeth.
And if it is an erupted tooth exposed to attrition, then grind that one with this Indian steel file whose shape is as follows:
And let it be made entirely of Indian steel and sharp-pointed; and let it have many fine points like those on a file used to grind the tooth little by little over several days with ease, so that no other teeth are harmed or injured. And when you have finished lining it up, straighten it with rubbing stones.
And if it is a tooth where one portion is broken off and causes the tongue to lisp, then you should grind away that part until its sharpness is completely smoothed over and flattened out so that the tongue does not stumble nor speech become impaired.
Chapter XXXIII
Concerning the restoration of damaged teeth with gold or silver foil.
When teeth are damaged due to concussion and removal by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot chew properly even after treatment with medicinal astringents, then you should fill those that are stricken with gold foil and not silver, because silver turns green over time and can tarnish in just a few days, whereas gold never changes.
And let the foil be in such fineness and thinness according to the amount that can fit between the teeth. And the method of placement is as follows: take the foil and fold it in half lengthwise between two healthy teeth, and then wrap it around with two twists between the damaged teeth or just one if there are fewer, until the tissue reaches the sound part of the other tooth. And then press down firmly on that side where you began, using your hand with ease and skill so as not to damage the tooth.
And let your pressure be such that you secure the foil tightly between the roots of the teeth so that it does not become loose or dislodged.
And then trim the excess edges of the foil with forceps or scissors, and gather them up in each place with plaster, covering them up between the sound tooth and the damaged one so that they do not cause injury to the tongue. And then let it remain thus for three days.
But if it becomes loose or broken, reinforce it with more foil in this same manner whenever necessary.
And this is the method of preparing teeth and the technique for restoring two sound teeth and two damaged ones, as shown in these illustrations:
And when it happens that a tooth or two are displaced by their own falling into their proper places, and have been restored as we have described, but still remain loose,
Then only does this happen to skilled and knowledgeable artisans.
Sometimes it happens that some of the bones of cattle are apt for this purpose, and they are fashioned into the shape of teeth and placed in the location where the tooth is missing, and secured as we have described, remaining in place and serving well for a long time.
Chapter XXXIV
Concerning the incision of the frenulum which causes difficulty in speech.
This frenum, which attaches the tongue either naturally or accidentally due to scar tissue that has formed, may sometimes obstruct speech.
The operation is as follows: have the patient open their mouth while they are sitting upright with their head held still. Then lift up their tongue and cut that nerve frenum according to its width until the tongue is completely freed from its attachment.
But if there is hardness or firmness in that place due to scar tissue from an injury, then use tweezers and cut through it lengthwise until you have completely severed the frenum and dissolved the adhesion.
Be sure not to make a fissure in the front of the flesh, and avoid cutting too deeply or causing bleeding.
Then rinse the wound with water or vinegar or warm water, and apply a bandage to the tongue. Tell the patient to keep their tongue away from that side for several days so that it does not heal again in that place.
But if bleeding occurs, apply a lint bandage soaked in nitric acid to the area. If the bleeding continues, then cauterize the location with a silver nitrate cautery as appropriate for this situation. And then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Chapter XXXV
Concerning the removal of a ranula from under the tongue.
Sometimes, a tumor resembling a small mollusk develops under the tongue and interferes with its normal function. This can grow large enough to fill the entire mouth.
The procedure is as follows: have the patient open their mouth facing the sun, then examine the tumor.
If you find it to be of dark or black color, hard, and insentient to the patient, then do not touch it as it is a cancer.
But if it is fluctuant and white, then use tweezers to compress it and cut through it with a fine scalpel, making sure to cut all the way around. If bleeding occurs during the procedure, apply a lint bandage soaked in nitric acid to restrict the flow of blood.
Then return to your work until you have completed it with care, rinsing the area with vinegar and salt. Then treat it with other appropriate remedies until it is healed.
Chapter XXXVI
"Of removing an abscess from both ears and that which is located in the navel, as well as other abscesses."
"When an abscess occurs in the navel, it is called a gland that forms sometimes there. It happens externally and is named 'both ears'. If you cure it with what we have said in the division and it does not heal, then consider if the abscess is hard, dark-colored, and insensitive to touch; do not touch it with iron."
"If it is of red color and the root is large, then do not touch it with iron due to the flow of blood. Rather let it ripen inside, and then you will draw it out or else it will break open by itself."
"If it is white in color, hard, and its root is thin, then it should be incised."
"And the operation in this case is to consider first whether the abscess has already ruptured and healed completely with rest or if it has decreased somewhat. Then make the incision before sunrise, with the patient's head towards the east and their mouth open. The assistant should take a clean cloth and press the tongue of the patient gently with an instrument called the 'mouth holder,' which is shaped like this:"
"And it should be made of silver or brass, and it should be sharp with a knife."
"Then when you press the patient's tongue with that instrument and expose the abscess, cut it with your knife very gently. Then take a forceps and grasp it and put it in the wound, and pull it outwards as much as possible." "After that, if you pull out some of its tunics, then immediately cut them with this instrument whose shape is like this:"
"After that, if you pull out some of its tunics, then immediately cut them with this instrument whose shape is like this:" "It resembles a forceps, but its extremities are curved so that the points of each one face towards the other, very sharp. It should be made of iron carefully engraved."
"But if this instrument is not available, then incise it with a scalpel whose shape is like this: It should be sharp on one side and not sharp on the other."
"And after you have made one incision, make another according to this same manner of incision. Then wash the wound with clean water."
"But if there is bleeding from the wound, wash it with water decocted from oak bark or myrtle leaves and other astringent substances to stop the flow of blood. Then treat it until it heals."
"And sometimes other abscesses appear near those two ears, and you should incise them according to what I have said about the incision of two equal wounds."
"And I already treated a woman who had an abscess that appeared on her throat, which was dark in color with little sensation. She had closed the wound herself and was breathing with great difficulty, and she had been prohibited from eating or drinking water for several days. She was already near death if not treated within one or two days."
"And the abscess had swollen so much that it had formed two large lumps, which discharged through two holes."
"So I opened it with forceps and gripped one of them, and pulled it out. A large portion of the abscess came out, and then I made an incision where I understood the other hole was, and I opened her mouth and pressed down her tongue, and then I put a forceps in that abscess."
"And then you should cut off a large part of it, and if there is not much bleeding from it." "Therefore the woman's throat was completely healed, and she immediately began to drink water and eat food. However, I continued to incise that abscess many times over a long period of time, and it succeeded in forming another abscess in its place, which elongated that incision."
"So I took hot water and cauterized her throat, therefore stopping the addition of new flesh. And then she walked around, and I did not know what God had done through me."
"Chapter XXXVII."
"When the navel becomes inflamed."
"When catarr descends to the navel and it becomes inflamed and elongated, at times it is called perpendicular; but if it is thick and round at its base, at times it is called 'bubble'."
"If the inflammation is cured with what we have said in this division and your treatment does not confirm it, and especially if an abscess has already burst open and become thin, then you should incise the one that is aggregated roundly. And if it is as long as that, and there is bleeding of dark or black color, without any sensation at all, then you should beware of this incision, for in such cases there is fear about the patient's condition."
"And when you find that according to the manner I have described of its whiteness and length, you should make the patient lie down and press the tongue of it with an instrument which has been prepared for that purpose, and hold the onyx in the new wound, and pull it downward and incise it with one of two instruments which are mentioned in the incision of double mellas."
"And you should not incise it unless what is appropriate to its natural term without addition, for if you incise more than that, you will harm the patient."
"And after the incision, use what has been recommended in the incision of double mellas, and care for it until it is healed."
"But if the patient is frightened by the incision of it, you should use a hot iron in its cauterization without fear, and the manner of cautery in it is only with sharp water, which is that you hold the head of the patient on his right side, and then press the tongue of it with the instrument which has been mentioned, and take some of the water which has been mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and apply it with a live coal, pausing it neither thick nor thin, and from it fill the cavity of the instrument of which this is the shape:"
"So that the extremity of the cavity in which the medicine is placed is like the cavity of a spoon of ray, and pause the instrument with the medicine over the ulcer, and the patient should lie on his side so that saliva or mucus from the mouth does not fall into the interior of it through the intrusive medicine, lest it cause any harm to him."
"And then you place your hand on the medicine and squeeze it over the ulcer for about half an hour until you see that it has become blackened and dried by the biting of the medicine."
"And if you wish, take some cotton and wrap it around the extremity of the ray, and immerse the cotton in the medicine, and insert the ray with the cotton into a cannula from above until the cotton adheres to that cannula, and do this several times until you achieve what you want from the cauterization of the ulcer, and then leave it alone for it to dry and fall off after about three or four days."
"And if you need to repeat the medicine, repeat it, and after cauterization cleanse around the ulcer with cotton soaked in honey, and remove what is on the circuit of it from the medicine, rinse it with warm water, and then treat it externally with embrocation, and afterwards wrap it up until it has healed."
"And this type of treatment should be used with caution, incision and cautery should not be feared."
"Sometimes the uvula is cured with something more subtle than cautery and incision, for it is treated by suffumigation in this manner: take calamint, hyssop, origanum, rue, scabious arabic, chamomile, broad-leaved plantain and similar herbs of that kind, and adjust all those herbs, or some of them, in a pot, and immerse them in sour wine, and boil it; and the pot should be well covered with decent lutum, and in the middle of the pot there should be a tripod on which is placed a concave instrument made of silver or brass."
"And insert the extremity into the mouth of the patient so that the vapor can reach the uvula above it until the uvula is well suffused."
"And repeat this several times until it is dry, and be sure not to perform this treatment at the beginning of an eruption of abscesses, for that would stimulate the abscess too much, and you should not do that, but rather perform the treatment for the declaration of the abscess of it."
"But if you do not have this instrument at hand, then take a reed and make a closure of wax at the extremity of it, so that the mouth of the patient may be covered, for the closure of wax prevents the vapor from burning the mouth."
"And this treatment is good for health."
"Chapter XXXVI"
"Of the extraction of thorns and of what adheres in the throat, and of other causes."
"Often adhesions are found in the groin or spine of the foot due to some other cause."
Then you must remove what is apparent of it, upon which the sight falls, because when you press with the tongue on an instrument before the sun, it will be declared to you what is in the groove.
And what is not apparent and is hidden in the groove, you must make the patient vomit before the food has digested in the stomach, because very easily the cause attached to the groove will be forgotten by vomiting; or have the patient swallow a piece of bread dipped in oil or lettuce juice, or give them some dry breadcrumbs mixed with honey and salt; or take a piece of dried sea sponge, squeeze it well with wine, and have the patient swallow that, because when it gets to the place where its spines are extracted, they will be remembered then. **Chapter XXXIX.**
Of the Extraction of Sanguisuga Attached to the Throat.
When sanguisuga is applied with what we have mentioned in the division of cure with medicines and it does not adhere, consider then at the throat of the patient in the sunlight, because you have prepared the tongue of it with the instrument which we have recommended.
Then if you see the sanguisuga, extract it with a small hook or with a gentle subtle movement accordingly.
And if it is not possible for you to extract it with that, then take a concave cannula and insert it into the throat of the patient, and carefully place within the concavity of the cannula an ignited iron brand, and do this several times (until the sanguisuga is dead and removed from the throat) and have the patient abstain from water all day.
And then take a vessel full of water, wet, and place the mouth of it upon that (the throat), and wash the mouth with it; and do not allow any cause to remain in it, and hold the water for an hour again with your hand, because the sanguisuga quickly feels the water.
But if it is not forgotten with what we have mentioned, then fumigate the patient with incense or with asafetida through the instrument which we have recommended in the fumigation of the uvula.
Do this, so that they may recover.
And here is another way of operation in fumigation of that: Take an earthenware pot with burning coals inside it, and cover the pot with a lid which has a hole in its center, through which insert the end of the instrument; then begin the fumigation above; place the patient's mouth on the end of the cannula, close their mouth so that the fumigation is not wasted until you know that the fumigation has reached the sanguisuga, because the sanguisuga will soon fall.
And if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times, and have the patient abstain from drinking, eat salty foods and drink water, and do not drink water; and thus it is necessary that with this regimen it should be forgotten.
And this is the form of the instrument with which sanguisuga is extracted from the throat when it is seen: It resembles forceps thus, except that there is some curvature in it: "The one placed on the pestle has an extremity like the beak of a stork, which is called a glove, sharpened with a file."
"The last chapter."
"In this one, the sum of the sermon regarding the opening and closing of apostemes is given."
"Apostemes are many species with many forms, according to what has been remembered about them, each one in this book."
"And thus they differ in perforation and section through two ways: one is by the means of gangrene, inserted within; and thereby we comprehend from moistures."
"And the second way is near the places where they occur, for gangrene occurring in the head is different from that in the buttocks; and gangrene in fatty tissue differs from that at joints; each has its own treatment through operation."
"And with regard to some gangrenes, it is necessary not to pierce them but rather wait for their maturation or completion of healing."
"And there are other gangrenes that must be pierced when they are hard and not ripe according to their completion, such as those near joints, for when gangrene comes near a joint, its nature is prolonged within what is in its circuit, and quickly the ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted, causing contraction of that limb. Or it may be near a main member, and if you delay piercing until it is ripe, there will be no harm to the main member. Or it may be near the anus, which should not be pierced unless it is hard and unripe, so that its opening does not extend into the inner parts of the anus and make a fistula." "But you must know the time for piercing gangrene, which is when it is ripe."
"And you should know that gangrene is ripe when there is cessation of pain and fever, and around the time of decrease in redness and pulse, and when the head of the gangrene becomes sharp, and other signs."
"And it is necessary that you know that the piercing should be made near to the gangrene, at a place where there is little pus coming from the swelling."
"And piercing should always be done along the length of the flesh or body, if gangrenes are located in the parts of the thigh or leg, and in places where there are muscles, tendons, nerves, arteries, and especially in places where reflection is not present; for those that are reflected upon, use piercing according to that member."
"But when the gangrene is in a fleshy place, it is better to leave piercing until digestion of it is confirmed according to completion, as we have said; for if you pierce it before that time, the course of the passage from it is prolonged and much filth flows out, and quickly its lips become hardened and its depth increases."
"But some gangrenes are pierced according to the width of the flesh or body when necessary, or according to what that member needs."
"And it is necessary that you make a small piercing in small gangrenes, and a large piercing with wide incisions or many sections according to the diversity of the size of the gangrenes."
"And there are other gangrenes in which the cord should be curved and cut when it is made, so that it is finished at once like bread dough, as was done with troches of dewlap and buboes."
"And of those that are incised with three angles in section; and there are those in which it is incised like the figure of a mitre leaf, as with gangrenes on the angle."
"And there are some in which round section and crescent section are used, similar to those."
"But that one to which gangrenes do not extend like lion's paws on the surface, it is necessary for you to pierce it with superficial or flat piercing alone."
"And when the gangrene is large and has collected much pus, it is necessary for you to pierce it but do not try to extract all the pus at that time. Extracting a part of it and then packing the gangrene the following day, extracting more each time until it is completely drained."
"And especially if the patient is an elderly person of weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old man in decrepitude, for the animal spirit is often resolved with the exit of the pus, and quickly the patient dies, and you operate thus."
"Therefore guard this chapter with great caution, and also the piercing that you make in these gangrenes, making sure to cleanse the wounds and consider whether the wound of the gangrene is small or has a flat section. If it is small, use linen or cotton dressings; but if it is large and the incisions of the piercing are many, then pause in each traction until they come together simultaneously."
"And if in the gangrene a part of the cord is cut off or curved in its circuit, it is necessary for you to fill it with old cotton or thread made from linen cloth, like when baking bread or cakes without moisture; and strengthen that on the third day; and then process it and cure it with what is necessary for other wounds until it is healed."
"But if bleeding occurs during your operation, then use a cloth wrung out in cold water and vinegar and place it on the location of the bleeding many times."
"But if the bleeding persists, it is necessary for you to apply regimen and cure and powders which have been recommended in many places of this book and division."
"But if it is during wintertime and the location of the gangrene has many nerves, then you should make a poultice with hot wine and oil and apply it to those locations."
"And if it is during summer and the locations are fleshy, then you should apply poultices made with water and oil or wine and oil, all of which has been cooked until the third day as we have said, and then drain the gangrene, cleanse it, and apply to its cure what is necessary for it until it is healed."
"And this is what is necessary regarding the knowledge of the cure of gangrenes universally; but according to the way of distinction I have already said how each gangrene should be cured specifically in its own chapter."
Chapter XL.
Of sectioning gangrenes that occur on the neck of the head.
In the chain of the small head, posthemas appear, which are species of knots containing tunics that are made by them; and their species are many.
And among them are pimples, and those contain moisture like lime. And there are those which contain moisture resembling dust, similar to them; and those that are stony, hard.
And in the section of all, and in the extraction of these there is no fear, since the extraction of them does not cause harm to the art.
And the operation in section of those is that you should spread them with an instrument whose shape is like this [drawing], called entromes, until you see that it contains.
For if what it contains is moisture, then immediately cut it with a section along its length into a surface section according to this shape:
And begin at the section of line .B. up to line .G. Then, once the moisture has been evacuated, immediately you should excoriate that by which that moisture was contained, and do not leave any cause of it, because viewed troops return if there remains any cause.
And quickly immerse it in Egyptian cement, if available, and if not, in water and salt. Then fill it with that and leave it for another day, because with this you will corrode all that which remains of that skin layer.
And again apply that cement on it second and third times if necessary, until you are confident that there remains no trace of that skin layer. Then cure the wound with ointment until it is healed.
"And if an abscess contains fatty knots, then you should incise it in this manner:" "And if the section has a cross shape, then insert your needle between its two lips and cut it completely,
"If your arrow should go awry, then do what I have told you first."
"And similarly, perform the operation and treatment of an indurated ulcer according to what we have told you; for incision over an indurated ulcer is easier because it involves less blood and fluid."

Chapter LII
Of the treatment of inflammation of the navel.
Inflammation of the navel can occur for many reasons: it may arise from fissures in the skin that is over the abdomen, and then the thread or gut may come out from there according to where the other ruptures are; or blood may flow into it from a vein or artery according to what has been said earlier, or because of constricted wind in it.
But if it is due to a fissure in the skin and the exit of thread, then the color of the swelling is similar to the color of the body; and there is little pain, but it appears suddenly in various situations. And if it is due to the exit of the gut, then its situation with regard to that which has been mentioned earlier is one of very great diversity, and when you press upon it with your fingers it disappears, but quickly returns; and there is much pain associated with it, and a magnificent quantity of bath water and violent effort are required.
But if it is due to moisture, then there is little pain, and it does not disappear when you press upon it with your hand, nor is it contracted or swollen.
And if it is due to blood, then the swelling appears with these signs declining towards blackness.
But if it is due to raw flesh, then the swelling is hard, thick, and tough, and fixed in place according to its quantity.
If it is due to windiness, then his touch is lion-like.
If the swelling of the navel is due to blood from an artery or vein, or windiness, then you must be prohibited from treating him, for in that case there is fear and apprehension as has been taught in the chapter where it says concerning ulcers by an artery or vein.
And if the swelling of the navel is due to bile or tissue, then you should command the patient to hold his breath while standing upright and extend his body. Then take a tent and probe around the entire navel, and next, command him to lie on his back between your thighs. Next, encircle with a wide spatula in the area where you probed with the tent; then extract the contents of the swelling upwards using a large hook; finally, ligate it with strong flax or thread in an appropriate manner.
And next, hold the middle of the extracted swelling on the thread and insert your little finger into that opening and seek for the bile duct; and if you find it and hold it with the thread, then gently extract it and push it back into its place inside the belly.
And if you have found tissue, then take that with a hook; and cut away the superfluities of it.
But if it is against an artery or vein, then encircle that area and return to your operation. Then take two needles with strong threads attached and insert them into the circuit you have made around the swelling in such a way that they cross each other, making sure they penetrate well; then stretch the swelling in four directions over the needles.
And if you wish, remove the needles and let the location where the stretched skin was placed heal on its own. Or if it is thin, cut it when it has dried out and healed, and then dress the wound with something that promotes healing until it is completely healed.
And if the prominence of the navel is due to raw flesh in it or from moisture, then you should cut away the swelling as we have said and extract the blood or moisture which you find there. Then dress the wound with something that promotes healing and consolidates the location.
Capítulo LIII.
On the treatment of cancer
We have already said in the division of this book concerning cancer and its various types that it is treated with medicines. It is difficult to treat it by means of iron because it tends not to ulcerate easily; however, we have mentioned that cancer can develop from an untreated wound or sore.
And the ancients said that sometimes cancer can occur in locations where it is possible to eradicate it completely, such as when it appears on the breasts or scrotum, and especially when it first begins small.
But once cancer has become large and deeply rooted, it is not advisable to approach it because I have never seen anyone recover from such an illness nor do I know of any other treatment that could be effective.
And when cancer is located in such a way that it can be operated on, as we have said earlier, you should proceed by letting the patient's condition improve and purging them with black colchicum several times. Then, if there is a manifest swelling, excise it
And then prepare the patient for surgery by locating where the operation will take place. Then make an incision with a hook that is suitable for the situation, and carefully cut through all parts of the growth using the chain saw until there is no remaining cause for the spread of cancer. And let the blood flow freely, then remove it gently and squeeze out any remaining blood from the area. Then wipe away the thick blood with your hand or an instrument that you have at your disposal.
But if you have difficulty with thick blood flowing from a vein or artery, then cauterize that area until the flow of blood stops. Then treat the wound with other appropriate remedies until it has healed.
Capítulo LIV.
On the treatment of dropsy
We have already mentioned in this division the different types of water dropsy and their symptoms, as well as how they are treated with medicines.
And the type of water dropsy that is treated with iron is only the sole species of alithias. It is not advisable to approach this condition with iron treatment for the types known as tympanitis or hygrach because they are deadly.
And when you have treated this type of tympanitic dropsy with medicines and do not see any improvement in the patient's condition, then consider whether the patient has already reached a state of debility or if they suffer from another type of dropsy. If it is accompanied by other conditions such as coughing or abdominal discomfort, be careful not to treat it with iron because there is great danger involved.
But if the patient is strong and healthy and suffers from dropsy alone without any other illnesses or weakness, then the operation should be performed as follows:
"May be made of two pointed parts, long and sharp at one end like a sword; but it should have some shortening bit by bit, so that in the operation with it you do not penetrate into the intestines, and wound them."

"But if the generation of hydrocele is due to disease of the liver, then your section should be left of the navel by three fingers."
"And if its generation is due to the mesentery, then your section should be on the right side."
"And it is necessary that your section be made over the side towards which you want to draw off the superfluity, so that it may not flow into that part."

"And accordingly perforate the spermatic vessels within until the spoon reaches the desired place, and this is the place of water." "And accordingly draw out that and enter with an instrument whose shape is as follows:" "And it is like a thin silver cannula; it is made of silver or iron or laton, at the lowest part of which there is a small hole, and on its sides there are three holes: two on one side and one on the other side; and its extremity is cut obliquely in the manner of a feather, thus:"

"But evacuate according to the quantity of his virtue, and consider also the disposition of the disease, the virtue of the pulse, and the goodness or badness thereof."
"And accordingly draw out the instrument and retain the water which is kept back by the cord, which retains the hole that you made over the spermatic vessels which I have told you to perforate in this manner."

Capítulo LXVII
On the treatment of hemorrhoids.
Sometimes, rupture occurs in the hemorrhoids as we have said, and it becomes inflamed.
And do not give any laxatives to the patient without cause; if you do give them, it is little; and they return in all hours.
But if the time is prolonged with that, it makes an anal fissure in which the intestine opens into the anus; and this happens because of the extension of the anus which is in the hemorrhoids as we have said, which causes the anus to stretch, soften, and become inflamed and swollen.
And its cure is with cautery, as will be described later in this book.
And sometimes it is cured with iron according to this method: and that is for the patient to sit on his heels between two stools, and then dry the area of the rupture of the swollen abscesses with a cut made horizontally according to its size.
And then stretch the anus white which is below the spine so that it is exposed.
And then take a probe and place it on the most prominent part of the anus, and press it against the front of the abdomen.
And then cut both prominent parts on either side of the probe's end in the anus, and join them together with a suture.
And then extract the end of the probe, and do not insert anything into the anus at all, nor extend it further, nor any other cause as you will know better in the treatment of intestinal hernias.
And then treat it with the treatment for piles, and when you cut the veins, cleanse them and restore the pile so that it is consolidated; for the anus contracts and the prominence of the rupture does not remain.
And cautery is better in this place because it is closer to health.
Chapter LXIX
Of the softening of the scrotum's cord.
Many times the scrotum's cord in some men is softened because the flesh that is between it is softened, and it is noticeable by its appearance.
Then it is necessary for the one who is to treat him that they make the patient lie down on their side, and remove all clothing softened over the natural skin; and then join two lips with stitching.
And if you wish, at first the excess of softened skin can be removed with three or four cuts and firm stitching.
And then cut between the stitches, and also treat other wounds until they heal and discharge occurs.
Chapter .lxix
Of castration.
Know that castration is condemned in our law, but due to the request of certain people it has been written about in this book; and its remembrance is necessary only for two ways: one because it is within the knowledge of doctors when they are consulted regarding such things, knowing how to treat them; and the other way is that we often need castration of other beasts for our own use, as with dogs, goats, pigs, and similar animals.
And so it is said that castration is done in two ways: either by crushing or by cutting with a section.
But in that which is done by crushing, the way of performing it is that we seize the beast in cold water until its testicles become softened and lengthened and hang down. And then take them with your hand so that they are resolved and do not appear hard to the touch.
But in castration done by cutting with a section, you should hold the beast and press the cord of its testicles with your left hand.
And then lift up the suspending ligaments, and cut across each one with a section so that two openings result.
And then cut those which will appear to have burst open. "Ignore causes related to the liver, except for a subtle liver condition that affects the veins."
"This method of castration is better performed by crushing because strong crushing leaves no cause for the testicles to desire copulation."
"And appropriately treat the plague until it is healed."
"Chapter .70."
"On the cure of hermaphrodism."
"Hermaphrodism in males comes in two forms: one is when it appears as an empty space between the two testicles, where there are two testicles but a vagina-like opening figures between them."
"And sometimes urine flows from that spot which is in the chain of the testicles."
"In females, it is one type: when the vagina opens above the pubis just like two male testicles, slightly larger and thinner at the opening of the vulva, like the male penis and two testicles."
"And its treatment is divided into three types: two for males and one type for females." "And it is necessary that you insert those attached flesh parts so that the urine does not escape from there, and also heal them with care just like other illnesses."
"And in the second type of males where urine flows which is in the chain of the testicles, there is neither treatment nor operation for it."
"Chapter .21."
"On lentigo (freckles) and raised flesh caused by women."
"Freckles are naturally attached, they appear and disappear according to the weather; sometimes they are more pronounced in some women that they spread like in men and even during intercourse."
"Then you should remove the excess freckles with your hand or with oil and insert it."
"And do not make an incision in the end, especially on the front of the nose, to avoid bleeding."
"Then heal it with treatment for skin diseases until it is healed."
"But raised flesh is flesh that grows on the skin of the mother's womb and fills it up. It often resembles coal at its opening (and for this reason some first called it "cow's illness"); therefore we should remove it just like freckles, and heal it until it is healed."
"Chapter LXXII."
"On the treatment of a sore throat."
"A sore throat is when the woman's passage is not pierced or has a small hole." "And it can be either natural or accidental."
"Accidental is due to an illness that has preceded, and it is caused by excess flesh or attached skin, or thick and dense cicatrix."
"And it is caused either in the front of the womb or on its sides, or above or below it, and it prevents coitus, pregnancy, and childbirth. It often also inhibits menstruation."
"And the diagnosis of this condition is made by examining the uterus through the vagina if dilation is apparent. But if it is not apparent, you should examine it with your fingers or with a probe."
"But if the dilation is due to a thin cicatrix and it is apparent between the two lips of the vulva, then cut it and tear it apart."
"And if it lies on top of both labia majora, then gently press your fingers together from both sides towards the middle."
"And let the woman lie on her back with her legs extended. Then gently spread both lips with force until that thin cicatrix is broken and dilation is achieved."
"And then take some wool dipped in oil, place it on the location, and leave it for a day so that the area does not stick together."
"But if the cicatrix is thick and dense, then you should cut it with a broad-bladed knife or with a myrtle leaf."
"But if dilation is due to attached skin, then suspend that skin with oil and cut it."
"And use medicines that stop bleeding without causing injury, such as achiote and dragon's blood, and hyssop mixed with egg white."
"And then insert a wide lead cannula to ensure that the wound does not heal too quickly."
"And keep it like this for several days and apply poultices of linseed."
"And then heal it with other treatments to consolidate it until it is healed."
"And sometimes during childbirth other flesh also comes out, so you should cut according to this method." "But if this is due to a bone abscess, then do not use iron in any way on the bone abscess that is in the womb."
"Chapter LXXIII."
"On the treatment of hemorrhoids, prolapse of the rectum, and red tumor that occurs in the vagina of women."
"Hemorrhoids are a condition where multiple veins at the anus become varicose and continually bleed. And when these hemorrhoids become old, they hang down like grapes."
"And I have already spoken in the division about the species and signs of these hemorrhoids, and I will say now which ones receive treatment and which ones do not."
"So I say that hemorrhoids that are in the front of the womb and do not appear at examination should not be treated with iron."
"But those that are at the opening of the vagina and can be felt with the fingers are those that receive treatment."
"And you should place the woman in a warm bath and then gently spread her buttocks with forceps or rough cloth, and cut those hemorrhoids with razors."
"And then sprinkle powder from one of the non-injurious cutting powders on those places where bleeding occurs, such as aloes and similar things."
"And then have her press her feet against something for an hour, and then place her in warm water."
"And if bleeding persists, then have her drink a decoction of suma and the rind of pomegranates and citrons and similar things."
"And then take some barley flour, mix it with honey, vinegar, and wine, and make a poultice with this to place on her back."
"If blood is emitted, that is good. But if not, then apply two cupping glasses and perform scarification on the breasts."
"And then take wool and soak it in the juice of coriander or the juice of radish or the juice of garlic mixed with wine, and apply it to that place. And then treat that place with egg whites until it is healed."
"And treat it until it is healed."
"Chapter LXXIV."
"On accidental perforation of the bladder in the womb."
"Many species of abscesses can occur in the womb, such as bone spurs, stone-like abscesses, ulcers, adhesions, hernias, fistulas, hemorrhoids, cracks, prolapse, and other abscesses." "And I have already spoken about these diseases, the species of them, their signs, and their treatments in the division."
"And it is necessary that I say in this treatise about cauterization of an abscess that occurs in the womb when it is from those abscesses that become healed, and if you want to know how the operation of it with iron is done."
"Therefore, you should consider whether the pain of the abscess at its beginning is acute with percussion and swelling and fever. If it becomes red and if it is painful when touched, then do not cut it with perforation, but treat it with something that helps maturation until the sharpness of the symptoms ceases."
"And now you must place the woman upon a chair that has two arms; she should recline on her back and adjust her feet so they rest just below her belly, with her thighs spread wide. Then, place her arms by her sides in a way that is suitable."
"And then the midwife proceeds on the right side and administers the instrument with which the opening of the mouth is widened, the form of which will come forth in those cases that are about to be made."
"And when you want to administer this instrument, make sure it enters the mouth of the woman just until the point where the throat begins, and no further than that." "But if the instrument is larger than the opening of the mouth, then you should place powders on the surface of the throat so that the entrance of any instrument into it is prohibited."
"And it is necessary that you place a thread on the end of the instrument on the right side and above, so that when the midwife administers the instrument she may hold onto the thread and rotate the thread inside until the opening of the mouth is widened."
"And when the birth emerges and it is touched by the hand and is wet and soft, then you should catch that one with your hands using the spatula made of latten."
"And when the placenta is expelled, then you should place in a dish submerged in rose oil or verdigris oil which has some astringency and place it at the section of the throat."
"And then cover the mouth and over the vulva put clean wool submerged in water in which mallows have been boiled."
"And then it should be treated again two days hence, using this remedy that should suffice to heal it."
"And sometimes the wound and the inflammation are washed with a solution made of water and honey, or water in which iris root or long-rooted artichoke has been boiled, and then it is returned to the remedy."
"If the inflammation is inside the wound, it is forbidden to treat it with iron; then one should use the remedy mentioned earlier in this section."
"Chapter Seventy-Five"
"To teach midwives how to treat the drunk woman who is pregnant, when it presents itself abnormally."
"It is necessary for the midwife to recognize at the beginning the figure of a normal birth through its signs, namely when she sees the woman pressing her thighs and desiring to smell the air, and then she feels relieved by that which comes over her from below, and the expulsion of the child is hastened, she knows that this birth is according to nature's figure, i.e. the child comes out upon its head, and the second one either suspended or hanging from the navel."
"So when you see these signs, it is necessary that the woman's belly be pressed so that the embryo comes out gently, since when the first one comes out upon its head, the second one will follow, and it should be cleaned of those impurities with good cleansing."
"But if it is another than this birth is unnatural and blameworthy, for when the child comes out upon its feet and its body emerges before its head, and its feet are out first, or one hand comes out first, or a foot, or even the head with one arm, then it turns violently onto its neck, these are like those figures that are not praiseworthy."
"Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in all these matters, so that she may guard against error and deception."
"And I am showing you here the figure of those [birth positions], and what kind they are in each one, so that it may be indicated by this and understood."
"When the fetus comes out upon its head by natural impulse, and it is violently expelled from the woman and difficult to bring forth, so that her strength is already weakened, then one should do this: let women hold her and evaporate the pain of her womb with fennel cooked with honey and moistened with olive oil."
"And accordingly the midwife should insert her finger between those little lips and tear open with it the second one or break through that with her nail which is inside where there is humidity." "And press the woman's belly so that she expels the fetus."
"But if it does not come out, then it is necessary to lubricate the woman with mustard plaster and fennel plaster with honey."
"And accordingly command her to be pressed and make her sneeze with incense; and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour, because the fetus will soon be forgotten."
"And if both legs of the fetus are forgotten at the beginning, then it is necessary to reduce them little by little with ease." "But if it does not obey the assistance, then place the woman upon a stool and lift up its legs, and strike the stool against the ground, so that the woman may not fall due to the concussion."
"And if the legs do not turn back and the fetus dies, then incise those [legs] and remove the afterbirth of the fetus or tie its body with cloth and remove it gently because that will be forgotten."
When the patient lies on their back, then you should press those legs upward, and promptly turn the foot slightly inward, and then tie that up, and promptly take one of their feet and extend it little by little.
Once he is inside the space [between the thighs], then you should command him to press down, and make that sneeze with certain conditions, because sometimes they forget if God wants it.
And if he doesn't forget what has been said above, then you should gradually return the foot to its natural position until it stops, because sometimes they forget with light pressure.
And if all that has been said above is prohibited, then take some ground aloe and dissolved gum, grind it well in the mortar with good percussion, and promptly apply it to the woman's womb, the lowest part of her belly. And promptly make her drink water infused with dillseed, until she obtains relief from her hypochondriac condition.
"And sometimes when the parts are left uncovered by him, then he should undergo fumigation with myrtle and rest upon it." "And when the fumigation lasts an hour, then you should make him sneeze over a cloth, and at that moment, remove it from his mouth, and press the lower part of his belly with gentle pressure, because the wind is quickly forgotten."
Examination of the lateral folds of the buttocks with one of his buttocks. If you cannot reduce it with your hand, then elevate the woman's hips and make her bear down.
And if she cannot bear down, then have her lie on the bedsheet, and strike his buttocks vigorously with your fist, and then administer laxatives composed of honey or mucilages.
And if the birth is imminent, then have her sit upon a chair and then examine the reduction of the hand, and push out the feces according to its natural form using gauze, and make the woman sneeze and command him to press upon himself until the feces are fully expelled.
Examination of the feces on his colon as his buttocks are spread and his mother's fascia is on his back. That the midwife should have her hand inside the child and gently rotate it, facilitating its passage.
And when that has been done and as much has been pushed out, then pause upon the child's fundament with what we have recommended of oil and mucilages.
And then command him to move his buttocks little by little, and when you have done that, then have her sit upon a chair and command her to lean over the right side, and then command him to press down; and make her sneeze with a condition. Exit of the child prepared on its side.
When they make horrible faces at you as per this method, consider that and then insert your second finger with your nail into the fundament until it has been emptied of fluid.
And if the child is suspended upon its face and colon, then insert your hand into the belly, so that it may not be retained and die.
And then push the child out through its passages little by little until it is born, and command the woman to press upon herself several times, and may he be expelled with gentle examination if God wills it.
Exit of twins or multiple fetuses Know that many times twins are born, and sometimes three or four, but this is rare and unusual. It has natural causes and does not happen often.
And count them, even if they are multiplied, as one fetus, and separate them by chiasm, distinguishing those between the ligaments in the navel of each. And sometimes they are expelled just like one fetus through gentle natural examination, but sometimes they are expelled through painful examination as we have recommended
And if some of them are difficult to bring forth during birth and they have come to what we have said about the unnatural figures, then cure them as we have recommended.
And if the midwife is subtle and does what she does with facility and subtlety, and patience, and is ingenious according to all figures as they are prepared for her by the art leading to health
Recollection of that which is formed in the matrix from embryos and aborted
Sometimes one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and even more than ten are formed in the womb, and I have verified that one woman aborted six, and another bore ten all formed. The cause of this was made known by the measurement of the glorious wise ones.
And all this should be in the knowledge of the midwife that she may know what to do in such a case, and therefore pause if it is necessary to do so.
Chapter LXXVI
Of the extraction of the dead fetus
When you care for the dead fetus as we have said in the division of medicine and it is not expelled naturally, and you see that force must be used with your hand, then consider if the woman is of sound virtue and does not have any of the accidents by which danger to her may be feared.
Then it is necessary that the woman should be placed upon the bed on her left side, and let her head rest in a low place and let her hips be elevated.
And the assistant should hold her from both parts, or lie on the bed with her, so that his body does not extend beyond the extraction of the fetus.
And then moisten the mouth of the womb with humid oil and mucilage of marsh mallow and fenugreek and linseed.
And then the midwife should anoint her hand with these oils and mucilages, and then insert her hand gently into the womb, and then search around with her hand for where the hooks are on the fetus.
The convenient places for this are: then consider if the fetus is prepared to come out on its head, and then place the hooks in its heels or in its neck or in its mouth or in its palate or below its beard or in its collarbone or in the places near the ribs or below the hypochondria.
But if it is coming out on its feet, then in the perineum or in the middle of the back
It is necessary to hold the hook with the right hand and pause its curvature in that place which is between the fingers of the left hand, and insert the hand gently and place the hook in one of those places which we have mentioned until it reaches the cause of birth.
And then pause and place another hook or the third one if necessary so that there may be equal traction and not too much extension according to its straightness alone.
And let it be moved in every birth so that the expulsion of it may be alleviated just as is done with teeth when they are extracted.
And it is necessary that between them the extension be softened; and if any part of it is retained, then it is necessary for the midwife to anoint some of her fingers with oil and insert them gently and turn around what has been retained.
Therefore if the birth of the fetus is difficult, then the hooks should be changed to another place where it may be pushed further out; and do this until the whole fetus has been expelled.
But if the hand becomes exposed before the other one and it is not possible to reduce it because of its curvature, then a cloth should be wrapped around that; and then extract it until all has been expelled, and cut it off at the junction of the hand or in the elbow.
"And similarly do in the other hand and both feet."
"If the fetus's head is large or if there is some constriction in the pelvis or if it is in the neck of the womb, then it will be necessary to insert between the aforementioned spines and split the head open and extract the waters, or else use an instrument called “alundat,” the shape of which will come along with the shapes of other instruments in the chapter that follows this one."
"And similarly do if the fetus has naturally a large head: and then it is necessary to insert this with forceps, or take hold of it with an “alundat” as we have said before; and afterwards extract the bones with forceps."
"And if the head is exited and is constricted above the pubis, then it should be opened up so that the fluid which is in the uterus may flow out."
"But if there are no complications or signs of imminent delivery, then you should proceed to extract the head little by little according to your ability."
"And if the lower part of the abdomen is inflamed or there is dropsy in it, then you must pierce it so that the fluid which is within may flow out."
"But if the fetus is lying on its back, then its attraction will be lighter and its direction towards the mouth of the womb will be easier."
"But if it is constricted above the belly and the uterus, then you must extract it with cloth which you will have wrapped around your hand, and cut open the belly and uterus so that what is inside may flow out."
"But if the other members are exposed and the head returns, then insert your left hand; but if the mouth of the womb is closed, then insert your hand into the lower abdomen and grasp the head with it, and pull it with those things into the mouth of the womb, and immediately insert a hook or two hooks, and pull it with those."
"And if the mouth of the womb is constricted by hard adhering clots which have occurred at birth, then it should not be troubled over that; but rather it is necessary to administer a copious evacuation of fatty humor." "And apply plasters and follow up the patient with waters that soften and moisten."
"If the patient is on their side, if possible it should be made flat; and let them be given what has been said for a live patient."
"And if this is not possible, then they shall be incised with scissors, and it shall be extracted."
"Ensure that no cause remains within the second one."
"And when you have completed all your operation, then administer what has been said about the cure of burns from which this may occur."
"If there is bleeding, then apply styptics in water and administer the other cure."
"And I have seen a woman whose fetus was dead in her womb, and immediately afterwards she became pregnant again, and the other fetus was also dead." "It happened that a long time after an ulcer appeared on his belly; it became inflamed inside the opening and began to discharge pus."
"And I was called in to treat him, but even though I treated him for a long time, it did not heal."
"Then I pondered on some causes that might have an attractive force, and pulled out a bone from him, but after several days passed, he pulled out another bone; and I was very amazed because there are no bones in the belly."
"And then I realized that they were the bones of the dead fetus."
"So I dressed the wound and removed many bones from it. The woman was then in good health and lived that way for a long time until one day she gave birth to a boy."
"And I do not affirm that this is strange, because in this there is knowledge and aid for the physician who works with his hand in treating."
"Regarding the shapes of the instruments necessary to extract the fetus."
"Form of treatment through which the main cause is opened:"
"This is the form of stretcher on which its ropes are tied, with two handles at both ends of each side." "It is necessary that this handle be made more slender and tight, and made either of ivory or wood."
"And let the width of each beam be two fingers and a half, and the margin of each one on both sides be one finger wide, and the length of each one is one and a half palm; and in the middle place of two beams there are two joints of that meter wood which are already fixed, whose length is more than one and a half palm, and the width of each one is two fingers or a little more."
"And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the main cause so that it can be opened with those when you turn the two specified handles."
"Another similar form but more slender and lighter:"
"It is made of ivory or wood in the shape of a forceps." "But nevertheless at the end of it there are two additions like these, and the length of those additions is two palms, and the width of each one is two fingers."
"And when you want to open the main cause with those, then place the woman on her back and lift the weights with your hands, opening what is between her thighs." "And then open your hand with the instrument like you do with pincers, grasping according to how much you want of the opening of the mouth of the main cause while the meter makes what you want."

"Regarding the extraction of the second cause:"
"When the second cause is retained during childbirth, then you should order the sick woman to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze with a condition, and press your hand over its mouth and nostrils, and if it comes out through this, that's good."
"And if not, then take a cloth and make a hole in it, and place it over those herbs burned on the mouth of the main cause, such as calamus, rue, anise, chamomile, saffron Arabic and lignum casia, and holy balm." "All these herbs or some of them should be immersed in water in the cloth, and place it on the fire."
"And then place a reed cannula in the mouth of the main cause, and hold it there until the vapor comes to the concave part of the main cause."
"And then make her sneeze as we have said, and the second cause will be expelled with speed."
"But if even then this cure does not work and it is not expelled, then you should order the midwife to immerse her left hand in sesame oil or in an emulsion of althea, and then insert it into the womb and search with that for the second cause. And when she has found it, then take it out little by little. But if it is attached to the front of the main cause, then insert your hand as we have recommended, and when you have found the second cause, extract it slowly according to rectitude so that the main cause does not suffer from violent traction." "It is necessary that they be moved on the right and left sides with ease."
"And if the mouth of the main cause is obstructed, we have already recommended the cure with sneezing and with medication of the cloth with herbs."
"But if it is not expelled with all the causes that we have recommended, then be careful not to tire yourself out in repeated attempts at extraction, but whatever comes out of her mouth should be placed on the thing of the woman, and then cauterize it with a salve and tetrafarmacon. For this will make it rotten right away and it will dissolve and be expelled."
"But when it putrefies, it produces a bad odor in the head and stomach, and this harms the sick person. And then remedies should be administered by fumigation and whatever is suitable for that."
"But some of the Ancients already used fumigation with narcissus and dried figs."
"Form of an instrument with which a woman is fumigated due to the retention of menses and second causes:"
"It should be made of brass or copper."
"And the subtle end should be placed in the womb and the wide end over the fire, and the fumigation should be placed on the embers of the fire."
"And hold it there until that fumigation is consumed, then repeat another one."
"Regarding the cure of the unopened anus during childbirth:"
"Many children are born with their anuses not opened, which are thin and closed." "So the midwife should perforate that ciphac with her finger. And if not, then perforate it with an acute spatula, being careful not to touch the nerve."
"And also place over that wool soaked in wine and oil. And also cure it with salve until it is healed."
"But if you fear that it is closed, then place a cannula in the hole for several days, and remove it when the child wants to defecate."
"And it has already happened that the anus became closed due to consolidation of a wound or an abscess. So then that consolidation should be incised and also cured with what we have said about cure and lead."
"Regarding the cure of fistulas that come from there:"
"The fistulas that originate at the lower part of the buttocks are usually large and thick, which originate near the anus outside or in the space between the two parts."
"And it is one fistula or several."
"And with that thickness being old and running with moist white humors or thin putrefaction, and sometimes there are some penetrating parts of these fistulas."
"And those penetrating parts are known by what comes out of them through exit and windiness. And sometimes the illness itself is used for exit, and often worms come out of them."
"And sometimes those fistulas have penetrating parts that go into the bladder and into the urethra. And those penetrating parts also go into the junction of the perineum and into the opening of the vagina."
"And what is known as a penetrating fistula that enters the anus and non-penetrating is this: you put your finger inside the anus, and carefully insert a thin probe of brass or iron into the fistula where there is not too much curvature."
"However, if there is tortuosity in that, then introduce into that narrow tent of lead or horsehair that you feel the tent or the hair on your finger."
"And if you do not feel anything with your finger and there is no evidence of obstruction, vomiting, or wind, as we have said, then you will know that it is non-penetrating, and you should cease treatment."
"And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or the meatus of the urethra, then its significance is urinary discharge from that and prohibition of it until the place is consolidated in medicine."
"But if it is penetrating into the junction of the hip or into the bone and accompanied by pain in the region, then its sign is that the tent has entered here if there is not tortuosity in the bone, and pain at the site of departure; and that afterwards there will always be putrefaction; and that nothing will help it, nor will it consolidate with ointment."
"And in all those penetrating fistulas there is no cure, and the cure of those is the labor and emptiness of the foolish physicians on which we put our faith."
"But in that one that is not penetrating and is not ancient, cure with iron is hoped for according to what I will recommend to you, and what I have already said."
"And it is that the illness goes between your thighs above its two sides and elevates its camber within itself, the hips are inclined towards its belly, and appropriately enters a lead or iron tent if there is tortuosity in the fistula, into which you should know where the tent has entered."
"And if that one feels the illness around the buttocks, then it is necessary for you to insert your index finger into the buttocks."
"If you feel the tentacle already inserted in your finger joint before the cut is opened, and if what you feel between your finger joint and that flesh is another thing, then know for certain that it has penetrated; and therefore do not work on that one, as it is not its function."
"However some say that it helps in some men's digestion."
"And of the treatment by which one hopes to be helped in this, it is that you burn cauterize subtly according to the width of the fistula, as is preceded, and insert that burning into the fistula until it reaches around the bone; and repeat it two or three times until you know that all those flesh that are fitted like a bird's feather quill have been scorched."
"And also cure it with hot compresses wrapped in cloth until all those scorched flesh are healed, and then cure it with medicines that generate and strengthen the flesh, and if it is healed, good. And if not, then know for certain that it will never be healed by any other treatment."
"And if the tentacle enters and does not penetrate into the anus that you have said is in the buttocks, and between that and the tentacle which is a thin membrane of flesh or skin, and sometimes the fistula follows along the surface of the backbone, then cut off the tail from the beginning of the fistula, and you will see it cut with the tentacle inside it, and let it be in the fistula until the section reaches where the end of the tentacle has reached, and through that tentacle it is freed and cleansed."
"And also cleanse those flesh fitted like a bird's feather quill, which have not been injured by any means."
"But if blood flows during your procedure while you are operating on those flesh, then millet it immediately and use a light instrument to cauterize with fire or with sharp medicine, for cauterizing with fire has two good habits: it is a scorching of those scorched flesh, and an incision of the blood and drying out of the humidity."
"And also cure it with hot compresses wrapped in cloth or in three-folds until the place is healed, and then cure the wound with hard flesh-generating and strengthening medicine."
"And these are medicines that have astringent and drying properties; when they are applied, it is restored and healed and there will be no recurrence."
"But if the fistula has already penetrated into the anus and is prolonged on the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the anus and feel it with that."
"And then if you find the tentacle and between it and yourself there is only a thin membrane of skin or flesh, and it approaches penetration, then it is not an operation to be done on it, but rather by means of faith and hope."
"And this is to be administered in one of three ways: either cauterize it as we have said; or dry it out inside until you achieve the concavity through which it is possible to enter with the catgut and perform the cure described above; and do not proceed with a section so that you do not injure the lappet containing the anus, and thus incur the sin of injury without intent. And also cure it with what we have said because even if it is strong, it will be healed quickly. Or stretch out that membrane and cleanse that pus which dried it inside near to the anus as we have said, either with a tentacle or with another instrument with a sharp point, and also cleanse those flesh fitted in the section until they are covered; and then strive to restore all the wound with a suture, and if the opening above is not healed, and the fistula remains open at the beginning of the anus, it will be easier for the disease to occur." "And sometimes the fistula is finished in this way: when you insert the tentacle into the fistula, and it appears on the side of the anus around the surface of the body with the chain and at the edge of the anus, then take a tentacle with a perforated extremity, which is like a needle for preparing hearts according to this form:"
