"And after he left me, he returned to his land and I heard that the man was prepared and had cut off his whole hand, and he was healed."
"And I do not now narrate this story except to be helpful regarding what can be said about this illness, and that it may have meaning according to which it is interpreted and acted upon."
"De cura sinuum et qualitate clisterizationis cum medicinis" can be translated as "On the treatment of diseases of the spleen and the quality of cleansing with medicines by enema". This phrase suggests that it is a medical text discussing the treatment of diseases related to the spleen, and the use of medicinal enemas in such treatments.
"When an apostema occurs in some fleshy members and the space of the apostema is prolonged until it collects pus, and then it bursts and perforates, and the pus is discharged from it, and the place remains void as if it were a vessel, and the skin that is above it appears like finely woven cloth, and it has not reached ultimate corruption, and does not print on bone or nerve or ligament, it is called 'sinu', and it is not called fistula."
"But if the space is prolonged until corruption prints on some member, then it is called 'fistula' and not 'sinu'."
"And the treatment of it is that you cut away that skin entirely as it is turned back over itself, especially when it is thin and made like cloth, so that it does not adhere to the place because of its corruption."
"But if you hope that the skin will adhere and that that corruption has not yet reached its ultimate conclusion, and there is some opening in the skin, then you treat it with an enema."
"And when you consider the sinu, if it is large and the arm that comes out has a fetid odor, then you administer an enema with the Egyptian medicine which is made of oil and vinegar and cinnamon received in equal parts, and they are ground together in a vessel, and cooked over the fire until the medicine becomes hot and reaches the consistency of honey."
"And then you take as much of that as is necessary and dissolve it with water and honey; and administer that enema to the sinu, and strengthen the opening of it, and leave the medicine in it for the duration of two hours."
"And then you remove that with a sponge; and do so for however many days are necessary until the sinu is cleansed and the corruption is removed."
"And sometimes an enema is administered with water of ashes when this medicine is not available; and you take the ash of vitriol, and place it on the water; and then cook that and administer that enema with it until you are assured that the sinu is now healed."
"And if the patient does not tolerate the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, then you administer an enema with warm water and honey mixed together with three parts cinnamon, and also administer it with wine and honey mixed together; for the property of honey is to cleanse and wash, and wine makes the sinu adhere, especially when there is excess of astringency and dryness in the wine."
"And when you do this sometimes and you are assured that the sinu has been removed, then you administer an enema with that which causes flesh to grow in it."
"And when you take of the ointment called diafinicon and dissolve it with sweet oil and astringent wine; or whatever other medicines and ointments you administer that have properties which I have already written about in the treatise on ointments."
"And if the opening of the sinu is narrow and the cannula of the enema cannot be received, then you dilate it with a small iron gradually, and pause in it with a hot cloth wrapped in Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it has been dilated."
"And similarly, if the opening is wide, then you gather together its lips with a suture and leave in it the amount which enters between the enema without addition."
"And if the opening of that from which the arm emerges is elevated above its parts, then you dry it at its base where it enters into it so that the arm may run freely; for when the arm is restricted by the narrowness of the sinu, flesh can be generated there."
"And if it is not possible to dry the sinu at the entrance of the os near its base as you wish, then have the member prepared with such preparation that the arm may emerge from it lightly according to your desire and that there is in it no cause for the arm to be retained."
"But that which is over the opening of the sinu, you remove it at all times so that nothing may be adjusted to the arm." "And in order that you may know whether that which emerges from the arm is much or little, or digested, or undigested:"
"And with this you also consider the place of that sinu, whether the patient feels pain there or not, and if there is an abscess."
"And when your treatment has been prolonged in this manner and you see that the matter which is poured over the opening of the sinu adheres or approaches adhesion, then you remove it on the third day, and when you remove it, then change the cloth for another and renew the ointment."
"But if the sinu is far apart from space and there is subtle virus, then do not despair of its adhesion, for its healing is near; for some people in whom flesh is slowly generated in their wounds, and among them are those in whom it happens conversely."
"And if from the sinu after many days an undigested arm emerges, then you know that the sinu does not adhere; and if the adhesion of the sinu is delayed and the cause is prolonged, then you apply medicines which are drying, and if the medicines are humid in their substance and virtue, they are dry like diafinicon ointment when there is excess addition of sage."
"And the last most effective thing with which it is treated is that you take diafinicon ointment and dissolve it in sweet oil, and mix it well with old wine in its substance, and then apply it over there and use it."
"And in that action, if there is no arm present, use diafinicon ointment mixed with honey, cooked until it thickens, or take myrrh and aloe wood and incense, triturate all of them and powder over the honey when it is hot on the fire, then line this over cloth and apply it over the sinu; and also line that with honey which you have cooked until it thickens, and powder over cloth."
Sometimes a long and rough broth of heaven's lilies (and it is the lilies of heaven) and flour of barley and centaurea is administered, and use those simples or adjust them, sieve them and sift them and powder them over the honey which has been recommended.
And if the wound is prolonged and not healed by this treatment, you will know that corruption has spread to the bone itself, and then you must investigate whether it has reached the joints or other hard parts or even ligaments. Then you should treat it with fistular cure, as described above.
Of the treatment of blisters and nails rubbed raw and cutting the tip of the finger added and sectioning.
A blister is an abscess that appears beneath the nail of the thumb or another finger and grows more quickly on other fingers. If it is prolonged its treatment is more difficult, either it is an abscess from a cauterized abscess, or it is corrupt and throws out pus which corrodes the root of the nail, and often the whole of it becomes corrupted, and often its corruption reaches the bone within, which then has a foul odor, and the tip of the finger becomes blackened, and its color becomes dark.
And therefore, when you have that which has been said in the division and your treatment is not effective, then you must incise with iron all the superfluity that remains of the nail, and immediately cauterize the wound with it, for cautery is very useful in this case.
But if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy, but the growths at the edges of the nail begin to compress the flesh within, and they start to pierce and cause pain there, then you must make a thin cut from the angle of the nail that pierces the flesh, and push it out and incise that flesh easily, and place over that which remains of the flesh medicines corrosive enough to remove everything; and immediately treat it with ointments until it is healed.
But if the corruption has already entered into the bone, then you must incise the bone there and extract it, for there is no time when the bone can be healed if it is corrupt.
And if the corrosion and corruption extend to the finger, then you must incise it at one of its joints according to how far it has spread, and immediately treat it until it is healed.
But if the nail receives percussion or attrition and there is intense pain in that place, then at the beginning you must bleed the sore, and immediately dry the nail with a sharp spatula with a transverse section from top to bottom, taking care that the section does not reach the flesh that is under the nail, for you will cause intense pain to the sore, and it will be the cause of the formation of excess flesh in that place; and immediately treat that place with something that relieves pain.
But a finger that is swollen, which occurs in many men, is usually all flesh and very painful to the bone, or it may be very painful in the nail.
And some of them are born at the root of the joint, or the formation is in some joints of these fingers. But that which is formed in some joints of the finger is not painful, but that which is formed at the joints is usually very painful.
And those that are born fleshy, the section is easy, and it should be incised there near its root with a wide spatula.
But that which is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; therefore beware of the amputation of it.
But that which is formed in the finger near the joints must be incised at the beginning with a round incision into the bone, and immediately saw it with one of those suitable saws for that, and immediately treat it until it is healed.
But consolidation which occurs in these between their visible veins or by the nature of the person who is born that way, or by consolidation of phlegm or by burning with fire, or by similar causes, then you must dry that consolidation until those fingers return to their natural form.
And immediately place between their bands of linen soaked in rose oil to prevent them from becoming consolidated lightly, and separate those, or place between those a thin sheet of lead so that they are consolidated according to what is necessary.
And similarly if consolidation occurs in some of these with the palm, then you must dry that consolidation according to what is prepared and suitable for the figure of the member.
Of incision of veins, there are two kinds:
Vices such as varicose veins are caused by thick, engorged veins full of melancholic superfetations which occur more often in the legs, especially among those who travel, work hard or carry heavy loads.
Then you should administer a purge of the black bile from the body several times with strong expulsion, and also bleed the patient from the basilica vein.
But the treatment of varicose veins with iron is done in two ways: one is that it should be incised and the black blood drawn out, and the other way is that the vein should be elevated and all of it extracted.
The procedure is as follows: first, insert a sharp instrument at the beginning of the vein with cold water so that the thick blood may be resolved and liquefied. Then, tie off the unhealthy part of the vein below the swelling using a bandage, and then cut the vein open wide in one or two or three places. Next, elevate the black blood from the vein at the upper end of the unhealthy part, using a tube, and draw out as much blood as desired, repeating this process several times until the vein is emptied of its harmful properties.
And then ligature that vein, and command the patient to abstain from foods that generate black bile.
And repeat the treatment by phlebotomy when the veins are filled again and it is necessary for the patient.
But the elevation of varicose veins is done in this way: first, remove any bandages from the affected area and then have the patient bathe and insert cold water into the vein until it becomes reddened and the veins are dilated. Alternatively, you may exercise the limb vigorously if bathing is not available, until the member becomes fatigued.
And then cut the cord in the direction of the vein on the right side at its length or at its end above the knee joint, or below it at the ankle.
And then tie off the cord with a ligature and strip away the vein from all around it until it appears at the surface of the skin. This should be done while the vein is still pulsating, because sometimes it becomes dark-colored after being tied off.
Then carefully remove the ligature and tie again with a white thread that is strong enough to hold together.
And then place some lint there until it becomes elevated and freed from the ligature, and suspend it with a linen bandage.
And then cut another section near that section three days later, and strip away the vein from its attachment above it until it becomes visible.
And then elevate that again and incise it in another section below the ankle, and then extract it from that section until it is emptied by the second section, and also extract it from the section that is above it.
And do this until you have extracted all of it from the section that is above or below all the sections, so that everything is emptied. Then stitch it closed.
And if you are unable to extract and elevate the vein completely, then insert a strong doubled thread needle into it and ligate it and remove it. Otherwise, place some lint there and roll your hand around it until it is expelled. And be careful not to cut into the vein, because if it breaks, it will become difficult to elevate and will cause harm to the patient through that injury.
And when all of it has been removed, then apply to the wound a dressing made of wool soaked in rose oil and unguent roseum. Cover this with another dressing and let it heal.
And if the vein is contracted and twisted in such a way that it has no straightness to it according to what we have said, then you must make incisions along all of its tortuous parts and at the points where it is adhered. Then suspend it with ligatures until you have elevated it completely.
And be careful when making your incision that you do not cut into the vein or damage it, because it will then be difficult to elevate. Use caution and skill in this procedure.
Form of the Incision with which a Vein is Cut:
"It is not sharp like needles and does not have a pointed tip so it will not pierce the vein. It has thick flexibility like that of a lion. If it were thin, it would cut through the vein due to its fineness."
"Removal of a leg vein."
"This vein is found in the calves of the legs, especially in hot lands like those inhabited by Arabs and in dry, arid lands with little tenderness where neither grass nor herbs grow."
"And it is also generated in other places on the body besides the calves."
"And its movement is one of putrefaction that extends from the spine like venom, coming from within the body, causing serents and worms to appear between the spine and the flesh."
"And a sign of the onset of this condition is inflammation in the calf, with swelling at that location. The vein begins to emerge from the site of that swelling, appearing like a plant root."
"And then when the vein appears at its end, you should take a piece of lead weighing as much as two dragons [an ancient unit of weight] and tie it around that area. Leave the lead hanging from the calf."
"And whenever it happens that some cause appears outside it, cover that with lead and leave it tied in place." If the condition persists, then cut off a part of it and wrap up the remaining; do not cut that which has not yet come out, for if you cut that, it will constrict and enter the flesh causing an abscess and putrefaction in the area leading to bad ulceration.
It is necessary that it should be treated slowly and extracted little by little, until it is completely removed from the body and no remnant of it remains in the body.
And some men have told me that this vein is as long as 20 fingers, and I have even heard that one man has had it as long as 30 fingers.
And if it is cut at the time of its treatment, then insert a probe into its track and pierce that with a long probe through the body until all liquid is evacuated from the matter, and apply putrefactive medicines to the area for several days; and afterwards treat it as you would treat an abscess.
And this vein sometimes has many branches, especially when it appears at the junction of the leg or in the leg itself, and it comes out with many openings; it is said that there are almost as many branches as openings.
And so treat it thus as we have said in its division, along with what has been said above.
On the section of worms generated under the skin, also called bovine disease
This disease is called in some lands the bovine disease because it often affects cattle and there are many worms that are born between the skin and the flesh, which crawl throughout the body and cause swelling of member after member until they break through the skin and come out.
And its generation is due to putrefaction of some humors, just like the occurrence of worms and serpents and earthworms and roundworms in the belly.
And it is feared because of its harmfulness, for when it goes into the body and rises to the head, then it often enters the brain and causes damage to it, and this happens very often.
And therefore when you wish to treat it and remove it, first find out its path and appearance through the senses, then take what is on top of it and what is below it with pressure and constriction, and then dry it off and pull it out.
And if it is embedded in the flesh and you cannot grasp it, then apply a cautery with fire to the spot where it resides, for its greatest danger is corruption of that area, as we have said.
And if it has reached the head near the brain, then press over the eyebrow with strong pressure and dry out that area, and remove it; and the patient should use medicines to cleanse their body of putrid, harmful humors, and avoid foods that cause putrefaction.
On the section regarding the disease known as "nafir"
This disease is called "nafir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes on suddenly in certain members of the body, and then changes from member to member.
And now I will tell you about it as I have promised you. I was called to see a woman who was ill in a village, and when I examined her arm, I saw a small inflammation on the vein of the arm. And after about an hour, I saw that inflammation move just as if it were a living worm crawling along, but more softly than it should have been, like molten silver flowing from place to place.
Then the pain went away from that spot and appeared in the muscle nearby, and then it remained there for about an hour.
And then it moved to the other side of the body and reached the other arm.
And she told me that it was moving throughout her body, as I had seen. And she was greatly amazed by its changes and the speed with which it moved from member to member. And I had already seen something like this in my own hands before, but I have not seen many people who can grasp the pain as it moves from member to member. But I did not see it so clearly with my hands as in this woman's case.
And I do not think it was anything but this because the woman was old, with dry skin and visible veins, and in this appearance to the senses there was that movable windiness.
And it is necessary that this does not appear according to its course in those who are delicate and have moist bodies with concealed veins.
And when you wish to treat it and the patient feels that pain, then do not grasp it with your hand as we have said, but press on it lightly and dry out that area where that blocked windiness has come out, and apply a cautery to that spot.
But if you cannot grasp it with your hands, then treat it by purging the body and using medicines that expel windiness. And apply plasters made from foul-smelling herbs and those containing serpentaria and similar substances.
On the extraction of arrows
Arrows are various in their species and also vary according to the parts of the body where they strike. For there is great diversity among them: some have large points, others small ones, concave or blunt points; some are solid. Some have three angles, others have tongues, while still others are star-shaped.
And the signs of an arrow striking the brain are: when it pierces the bone and comes out through the fontanelle, which is on top of the brain. This happens due to sudden violence, leading to blindness (scotomia), dizziness (vertigo), redness in the hands, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, vomiting bile, and severe difficulty speaking or loss of voice. And there is an exit point for white, powdery fluid like milk from the wound site, and it resembles the moisture of flesh.
And therefore, if these signs appear, then refrain from treating or attempting to extract the arrow, unless it is external.
But the signs of an arrow striking the heart are: it is near the left nipple, and there is pain where it has been driven into hard flesh, not soft. The movement of the arrow feels like a pulse, and black blood flows from the wound. There is sudden coldness in the extremities, followed by sweating and fainting; therefore, know that death will come suddenly without delay.
And the signs when an arrow has struck the lung are: frothy sputum of blood coming from the wound, and the vessels near the collarbone become congested. The patient's complexion changes, and they exhale with great force or pant for breath, demanding cool air to breathe.
And if the arrow strikes the pleura (the lining of the chest), then pain will be felt near the lower ribs. There is great difficulty in breathing with violent pain and sighing, and all the members are affected by muscle weakness.
"And if the arrow strikes the stomach, then swiftly remove from it any undigested food."
"And if the arrow enters the belly and remains stuck there, then some rent of the skin, or the flesh, or bowel may be torn; and there is little hope for recovery through the extraction of the arrow."
"And if the arrow strikes the bladder and urine is passed outside, and there is pain in the external parts, then you know that it is fatal."
"But other members such as the face, neck, throat, shoulders, arms, spine, collarbone, hip, knee and their corresponding limbs are saved according to the best practices when the arrow does not strike a vein or an artery and is not poisonous."
"And I will tell you what I have seen about these arrows, so that you may know how to treat them."
"It happened that an arrow entered the tear duct of a man's eye and I extracted it from the other side through his nostril, leaving behind the feather of the arrow in his ear, and he was healed without any harm to his eye."
"And I extracted another arrow from a Jew which had entered his eye through the upper eyelid, leaving behind the eyelid and extracting only a small part of it with which it adhered to its shaft, and it was a large pointed arrow of the Turks with a lion's head on it without feathers."
"And the Jew was healed and suffered no harm to his eye."
"And I extracted another arrow from a Christian man which had entered his throat, and it was an Arabic arrow with feathers on it. And then I incised over that between two guides and it was already submerged in the man's throat. And then I carefully extracted it and the Christian was healed."
"And I extracted another arrow from a man which had entered his belly and I thought that he would die because of it. And since thirty days had passed and there was no change in him due to its condition, I incised over the arrow and extracted it, and he was healed without suffering any great harm."
"And I saw a man in whom an arrow had entered his back and the wound had healed over it. And because it was about seventy years old, I extracted the arrow through the opening of the wound."
"And I saw a woman in whom an arrow had entered her belly and the wound had healed over inside her without any change in her condition. And the woman suffered no harm to any of her natural functions."
"And I saw another man in whom an arrow had entered his face and the wound was healed over it. And he broke off the arrow without suffering much pain, and appeared to be very brave."
"And I extracted the arrow from the nose of one of the king's princes which had entered into the middle of his nose and had already inclined slightly to the right. And the whole arrow was hidden."
"And I was called for his cure about three days after the arrow had entered him."
"And then I opened the wound of the arrow very tightly. And then I carefully probed it with my finger and did not feel anything; but he felt a pricking from behind the right ear. And then I suspected that this prick was due to the tip of the arrow."
"And I widened the opening with an ointment in which there is attractive and digestive virtue. By doing this, I knew that the place would be opened so that it would appear to me the place of the arrow and I could cut on it."
"And there was no significant injury where the arrow had reached that place. And I continued to apply the ointment on it for many days without causing any harm, and meanwhile the wound healed up and the swelling from the extraction of it went down over many days until one day he felt the arrow inside his nose and recognized this before me."
"And then I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for many days until it opened up. And with my finger I felt that and extracted the tip of the arrow subtly, which adhered to the shaft."
"And precisely I applied that corrosive medicine to the opening of the wound until I saw the tip of the arrow visible. And it took me about four months' time with this."
"And precisely when the wound was enlarged and I could insert the forceps into it, but it remained stuck and did not come out easily, then I continued subtly to pull and manipulate on it with various methods of extraction until one day I began to pull it out with forceps made for this purpose, according to what is described at the end of the chapter. And precisely I restored that wound."
"And some physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored. But I restored it and the wound healed up completely, and the illness was healed entirely without any remaining cause."
"And I recount to you the details of extracting some arrows because you should pause and consider this rule and meaning about what I have not said, since the parts of this art and its definitions are not understood by narration alone, nor is that book comprehended."
"And the skilled artisan says little about many things; and about what is present, he compares it to what is absent. And he achieves new operations and new instruments depending on the removal of foreign causes of the art when they occur."
"And therefore I say that arrows are not expelled from the limbs into which they have entered except by two ways: either by attraction of the place where it has gone in, or by the opposite direction of its path."
"And that which is expelled by the place through which it entered, or is an arrow proceeding in a fleshy location, and is attracted and expelled."
"And if it does not come out at the time when it was shot, then you should let it be for some days until the flesh around it becomes softened, and its attraction and exit may be facilitated."
"Similarly, if it is stuck in bone and does not come out easily, then let it be for some days and repeat the attraction and movement each day until it is finally expelled."
"If it still does not come out even after some days, then you should bore into the bone around the arrow with a subtle awl so that the place may be enlarged by the arrow and thus you can extract it."
"But if the arrow is already hidden in the location of the heart and is hidden from sensation, then you should seek it with a probe, and if you find it, then attract it with some instruments which are suitable for its attraction."
"If the patient's wound is too narrow and deep to operate on directly, and there are no bones or major blood vessels or nerves in the way, then open up the wound further until it is wide enough for the arrow to be safely removed."
"If one of the patient's ears is injured and needs to be removed, then carefully cut through all the flesh in which it is embedded using all the skill you can muster. Use all your ingenuity if you cannot remove the ear due to its fracture or torsion."
"When extracting the arrowhead from any location, use gentle twisting with your hand and forceps in all parts until you can grasp it. Use extreme care to ensure that the arrowhead is not broken and is easily extracted."
"If you cannot extract the arrowhead at that time, then leave it in place for a few days until the surrounding tissues have had a chance to heal. Then try again when the patient is feeling better." "If bleeding becomes profuse during surgery, then follow the procedures for treatment of hemorrhage as described in the chapter on wounds and injuries."
"And be careful when incising veins, nerves, or tendons. Use all your skill and care to extract the arrow smoothly and calmly, without hurry or hesitation, as I have instructed you."
"And once the arrowhead has been extracted, contract it to its original shape according to the figure indicated on the casing of the arrow. This is more helpful." "But if this is not possible, then do whatever you can based on the figures available."
"But when removing arrows that have been shot from behind, or when there is no wound channel present, or if the arrow has pierced through to the exterior of the body, feel along the path of the wound above the rib cage until you find the emerging point. Then grasp it with forceps according to its size and pull it out gently."
"But if the arrow is stuck in bone, then twist it gently in the opposite direction until you feel the arrowhead give way. Then push it further in and extract it."
"And if this does not work, leave the arrow in place for a few days to allow the surrounding tissues to heal, then try again when they have recovered."
"And if the shaft of the arrow is still inside, then push it further in with it."
"But if the shaft has broken off and you wish to apply traction, then insert a probe into the wound cavity and find the tip of the arrowhead. Then place it in the concave end of the probe and gently pull it out with the probe."
"But if the arrowhead is barbed or has a broad head, then forcefully insert an instrument into the wound cavity to push it back in, for such arrows are easier to extract this way."
"And if the arrow is poisoned, then it is necessary to excise all the flesh around the wound, if possible, and then treat the wound as appropriate."
"And if the arrow has struck bone, or entered the abdomen, bladder, or chest cavity and is close to vital organs so that you can touch it with your hand, then carefully grasp the arrowhead with forceps without injuring veins or nerves, extract it gently, and suture the wound if necessary. Then treat the wound until it heals."
"Method of extracting arrows using forceps:"
"Limbs like bird beaks seize arrows in such a way as not to let them go."
"Their grasp varies greatly: some arrows are seized firmly, others loosely, depending on the size of the arrowhead and its narrowness, as well as the width of the bowstring and the tension on it."
As rays pass through it, may it alleviate the pain within him in the hollow of his side.
Of phlebotomy of the veins
The veins of phlebotomy which are most commonly opened are 30, among which there are those in the head numbered XVI, namely two pulsating veins near the ears called "temporal"; two veins located in the temples appearing like herbs; and two veins located at the corners of the eyes called "canthi". There is also a vein prepared in the middle place of the forehead, and one which is at the end of the nose. Then there are two on the neck, and two veins on the upper lip, and two veins on the lower lip; and these are those called "angle" [veins]; and finally two veins behind the tongue. In the arms, five veins are commonly opened for phlebotomy: among these there is one cephalic vein which runs along the wild side of the arm; the people call it "the vein of the head". There is also a median vein called "sorda" composed of a branch of the basilica and another branch of the cephalic. The basilica is a vein placed on the inner side of the arm, called "cubitalis", which the common folk call "the vein of the belly". The funis of the arm rests upon the elbow joint and this is the vein commonly opened for phlebotomy. It appears above the pulse in a manifest way. The salvation vein is that which lies between the aforementioned auricular and the little finger; it has two branches.
In the foot and leg there are three veins: one of these lies on the outer side of the ankle joint on the wild side of the leg, another is the saphenous vein located behind the knee joint on the inner side of the leg. The third is the sciatic vein located behind the knee joint on the outer side of the leg. There are also other veins in the leg which resemble these.
The benefit of opening the veins near the ears is for treating ancient head colds, headaches, migraines and ulcers of the head from ancient times.
And the quality of letting blood from those veins is as follows: it should be done after removing the hair from the sick person's head. The head should be anointed with oil in the occipital region where both veins are located, using a wide cloth and good friction. Then tie the sick person's shirt tightly around their neck with a bandage so that both openings appear near the ears on two slightly elevated points of the head. Take hold of those with your index finger and if you feel the pulse there with your own finger, then proceed with caution.
Approach thou taketh the lancet scalpel, which is sharp-pointed, and thou insert it beneath the vein in the elbow until the phlebotomy comes to the bone. Then lift up thy hand with the vein and the elbow above and cut through the vein with an incising incision. And let the length of the incision be the size of two fingers or thereabouts, and cause as much blood to flow out as thou wishest.
Then apply powder and bandage it so that it may heal.
As was stated at the beginning of this book, some wounds are incised and cauterized.
Most of the two veins called arterial are to the temple, the help of phlebotomy is in ancient migraine and evil humors and frequent ophthalmia and sharp pains from excess fluid accumulated in the chest.
And the quality of phlebotomizing them is according to what I recommend to you: constrain the illness with a vein in such a way that both veins appear clearly under the skin and show their pulse, and then proceed gently.
Then lift up the elbow above the vein at its beginning with your little finger, insert the phlebotomy lancet into it, and raise up the vein thus; and incise it just as you did in the other two veins, and cause blood to flow according to your necessity.
Then release the constriction of the illness, and place your finger over the vein for an hour, then place cotton and powder and strengthen it above with a tight bandage, and leave it alone until it is healed.
As was mentioned before in the beginning of this book, the memory of these veins, their incisions, and their attraction.
And thus the help of phlebotomy of the frontal vein is especially useful for the cephalic veins in ancient illnesses of the face and migraine and rigor and fetid ulcers.
And the quality of phlebotomy of it is according to what I recommend to you: thus, the illness should be strengthened with a bandage so that the vein appears; and then take the instrument called "fossor", the form of which is this:
Place your finger on the prominent point that is at the head of the vein and strike it with a pestle or another tool in the manner you desire, allowing blood to flow according to the quantity you wish; then immediately relieve the patient's perforation and strengthen that area so it may heal.
And sometimes it is opened with a flebotomy knife, however it is not necessary that the flebotomy knife have an acute tip like other flebotomy knives, as long as its side edge is sharp; and thus open it crosswise, for the bone is close by and might break the flebotomy knife if it is thin.
But the benefit of these two veins that are near the lacrimal canals of both eyes is for the itching of the eyes due to heat and sebaceous matter in the eyes, and for illnesses of the face.
And the quality of bloodletting is that after the patient has strengthened their neck with a bandage, then perform the bloodletting, and you should be standing on the head of the patient.
And perform the bloodletting crosswise along the length of a little bit with a blunt flebotomy knife, for there is not much flesh in that location; and if the flebotomy knife is thin, its tip will break easily.
And then make the blood flow as much as you need, and pause on that spot, and strengthen it for one night with a bandage, and then remove the bandage.
But bloodletting from the vein of the nose is beneficial for acute fever and sudden sneezing, and for illnesses of the face and migraine and heat that occur in the face, especially when it is chronic.
And the quality of bloodletting from there is that the patient strengthens their neck and then places their nose in your left hand, and take a thin flebotomy knife that is long and place it in the middle of the head of the nose straightly, for the vein does not appear to the touch here, and because the blood begins to flow soon.
Be careful to gradually withdraw your hand with the flebotomy knife and make the blood flow according to your necessity; and then bind it for one night, for that wound heals easily.
But the benefit of bloodletting from both carotids is for the cure of dropsy and the beginning of leprosy, and for many illnesses and impotence and malignant ulcerations that are like herpes zoster.
And the quality of bloodletting from there is that each patient strengthen themselves on their neck with a bandage; and the operator stands over the head of the patient, and the patient sits on a seat.
And then bloodlet the vein along its length with an ample flebotomy knife little by little; and then remove blood according to a moderate quantity or according to what you estimate is necessary; and then do the same for the other vein.
And then remove the bandage and strengthen both veins with a middle ligature so that the patient is not fainted, and leave them like that until morning for the wound to be healed.
And the benefit of bloodletting from the veins of the arms is for small abscesses and pustules of the mouth and corruption of the gums and malignant ulcerations and fissures, and for malignant ulcerations that are in the nose and around it.
And the quality of bloodletting from there is that you make the patient sit in front of you, and strengthen their neck with a bandage, and then turn their lips and observe both veins of which one is on the right lip and the second on the left; and the demonstration of each is by its darkness, and more so because in the circuit of those there are small dark veins; and then cut each with an incisive incision.
But if there is doubt about which one it is, and you do not know which one it is, then you can make an incision in the largest of those, and from the manifest pus of those.
And do the same for both veins that are in the upper lips.
"Of the two veins that are left of the tongue, it is appropriate for phlebotomy to be performed on the cephalic vein at the forehead, and on the malady of the uvula, and maladies of the mouth."
"And the quality of phlebotomy to be performed is that which follows the malady between their hands in front of the sun, raises the tongue of them, and watches left of the tongue, one side of the vein and the other side of the vein, and the color of each declines towards blackness."
"And then phlebotomize each one; but be careful not to end your hand in phlebotomy of those who have arteries left."
"And the veins that are phlebotomized in the elbow are those in which blood usually flows in all men, and the phlebotomy of them is done according to two methods: either they put with the flebotomy lancet mirtle or olive oil of subtle inclination; or they cut with flebotomy knife, and call if necessary, and this is the form of it:"
"Let the side of it be like this: when veins are full and convex, it is appropriate to open them with an apparent large incision, and those that contain thick and turbid blood."
"And this flebotomy is of lesser width and more subtle point, and it is appropriate for phlebotomy of thin veins that contain subtle citrine blood."
"But the benefit of phlebotomy of the basilic vein which is one of three veins, is that it extracts blood from illnesses that are on the left side and neck, and from those that affect the feet and belly."
"And it is appropriate for the phlebotomist, when performing phlebotomy on that one, to guard well that one and be cautious about it, because there is an artery left of it; if he errs in adjusting the puncture of the flebotomy needle, he will cut into that artery and cause blood flow; therefore it is not appropriate to phlebotomize that with a puncturing flebotomy lancet, but rather cutting without tourniquet."
"And if the basilic vein does not appear by manifest appearance, then you should leave that one and move to another, or seek some of its branches; or you can phlebotomize in place of it at the end of the arm where it is manifest; and cut it with flebotomy tourniquet as we have said."
"But if you want phlebotomy of the median vein, then before the narrowness of the arm where you touch the place within that you know the pulse's place, and press firmly with your thumb on it; and raise the arm and cut the vein with concave incision with flebotomy tourniquet as we have said; and guard against hitting the artery by some space in the place."
"And when you compress with strength the limb, if swelling occurs in the place that you have pressed with your thumb, then that swelling is swelling of the artery, therefore avoid it."
"And if blood flows in the phlebotomy like urine of a child, and the blood is thin red, then you know that it is blood from the artery; then you stop and pause your finger on that for some distance; and then remove your finger, and if the blood stops, because many times it stops, then you compress the arm and leave that one."
"And guard against the wound of the incision, and be careful with it and do not move it for some days until it is healed."
"But if the blood does not stop flowing, and you see that there is no remedy for it, then you have cut into the artery; because the point of it is contracted, and the blood has stopped; therefore take some lint and fill that one, and press a linen bandage over the place of the vein with narrowing descent with limb and powders within another day."
"And then if the blood stops flowing, good. And if not, then cure it with that which has been mentioned before for stopping flow of blood."
"And the cessation of blood flow from it is difficult in many dispositions because of the smallness of the vein and the possibility of movement of the arm."
"But regarding the black vein, phlebotomy is beneficial for removing blood from the upper part of the head and from the left side of the body; because it is composed of branches of the basilic and branches of the cephalic, as we have said."
"And the phlebotomist should be careful in phlebotomy of that one because left of it is a nerve; therefore if he errs in adjusting the puncture of the flebotomy needle and touches the nerve, numbness will occur, and healing will be difficult, and sometimes it is not healed completely. And this nerve often appears at the sensation; and if it is hidden from some people and is thin and does not show up, then you should pause the flebotomy needle with which you phlebotomize with tourniquet incision, and avoid the nerve with your strength."
"And if the vein is between two nerves, then cut the vein along its length."
"Bleeding from the temple vein offers relief by drawing blood from the head, thereby alleviating headaches."
"Do you wish the phlebotomy to be performed with an olive-shaped lancet or a myrtle-shaped lancet? For it is safer than all other veins, as neither artery nor nerve is left behind."
"But even if a boil forms in some people after the first attempt at phlebotomy, do not strike it again."
"The first [consideration] is that you should know that phlebotomy should only be administered for the conservation of health and with hope and caution of avoiding illnesses, and that it should be performed on one of the veins in the elbow area, such as the cephalic, basilic, or median cubital vein; and that it should be performed at the beginning of spring, after fasting during spring and autumn, and around mealtime during winter, when signs ofpletion appear."
"And phlebotomy should be performed either on the third day or at least one hour after breakfast."
"However, phlebotomy should be performed whenever it is deemed convenient and necessary, whether during the night or day, at any hour and at any time."
"And children should not be phlebotomized until they are at least 14 years old; pregnant women should only be phlebotomized from the fourth to the seventh month; and elderly people who have already surpassed their sixtieth year of life should not be phlebotomized."
"And when someone wishes to be phlebotomized for any reason whatsoever, they should cleanse their bowels beforehand with a lion's-claw purgative; if there is much retained fecal matter in them, so that the veins do not draw the superfluities during the phlebotomy of the purified intestines, which would harm the principal members."
"And patients with sacred sickness and drunkenness should not be phlebotomized until they have recovered from their illness or sobriety. And phlebotomy should be avoided near colic pain, vomiting, and stomachache; and during multiplication of coitus, work, and exercise after fasting or vigils, or any cause that weakens the body or soul."
"And it is important to consider the subtleties of humors beforehand if the blood is thick; with foods and drinks, and with medicines if that is possible."
"And it is appropriate to take a bath beforehand if nothing prohibits it, or rather if one has been exercised for the sake that blood may be subtilized."
"And pause the phlebotomy before noon, especially around the hour of Terce, as we have said."
"And continue only if that part is protected from all animal accidents such as distress, anger, fear, and from all corporal accidents such as work, excessive exertion, coitus, and similar things."
"And at his seat, let there be present the causes used in the usual practice of men with aromatics and fragrances and balms and similar things according to their quantity."
"And let the phlebotomist sit on a cushion that is higher than the cushion of the person who is to be phlebotomized."
"And let him first extract his arm and rub that with his hand the phlebotomist two or three times; then let him strengthen the limb with a bandage and wrap it twice."
"And let the bandage be tied moderately, for if it is not equitable or if it is with superfluity, then it hinders the flow of blood; or if it is too loose, it hinders the course of blood entirely."
"And after tying off the bandage, let the person to be phlebotomized rub his hands together until the veins are engorged and clearly felt."
"And let the phlebotomist anoint his lancet with a little old oil specifically; then pause his left index finger on that vein where he wishes to perform the phlebotomy so that the vein may swell slightly and he may feel which vein he should pierce for blood flows from veins like strings under the skin, and it is also important to avoid those veins that are full of windiness because when one presses the lancet upon them they contract beneath the lancet."
"Therefore, let the phlebotomist be firm and attentive to all these causes."
"And then pause the lancet if the vein is filled in one stroke, that is good. But if not, repeat this another time nearby there or on it with haste if the location is not inflamed."
"And if the location is inflamed or the illness worsens, then let it be left alone for a day or two and do not tighten the bandage, because that would draw out an ulcer. Nor should one take a bath."
"And repeat the phlebotomy if necessary."
"And if the incision is small and blood flows subtly, and you fear that not enough blood will flow out, then repeat the lancet in that same furrow according to correctness and adjust the aperture slightly, but do this quickly before the location becomes inflamed because many people become inflamed with a small opening."
"But if the location is already inflamed, then do not repeat upon it because that will serve no purpose. Rather, pause on some part of the oil furrow for that alleviates the course of blood." "And it is better in this location to use oil than any other oils."
"Similarly, administer an oil furrow in all phlebotomies where veins are pierced with the prohibition of blood flow, and they do this with Tyriaca Alfadoc and Sagzenea when pausing on one of those over the location because blood is subtilized and revolved when it is thick."
"And if a large ulcer is generated in the location of phlebotomy because many times this happens, especially to those who have not been bled for that day or whose vein opening was small, then coitus and pause upon the location with a sponge infused in water and salt slightly scalded, and tighten it there for an hour because it will be dissolved."
"And this should be done immediately after the letting of blood from that vein with the completion of it or another vein."
"If there remains in the location for some days a blackness or greenness, do not heed this. But if you wish, pause upon it with some cause of Aloes and Myrrh dissolved, or some cause of mint juice or chamomile or similar things."
"Many times ulcers and elevations occur because of phlebotomy at the basilica."
"Therefore pause your hand upon that [the ulcer], and if you should press too much with your compression, then that elevation is harmful and bad. And therefore guard yourself to pause upon it with some cause of what we have said because much blood flows from the artery."
"The affected area should be made rigid using a plaster containing an astringent substance to toughen it. Then treat this with another remedy until healing is achieved."
"Remove blood from every person according to their strength and the prevailing color above their blood, as it appears."
"If the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red. Similarly, if it appears thick, allow it to flow until it becomes thin. Likewise, if it is sharp, wait until its sharpness is relieved."
"For those who are full and strong, and require bloodletting at one sitting, the vein should be opened widely, and the incision should be long."
"In the case of the lean person, do the opposite. Bloodletting should be done in several sessions and the opening should be narrow."
"The best way to perform bloodletting from a vein is through a transverse cut, not a puncture."
"This method of bloodletting is safer from bleeding and injury to nerves. It is more praiseworthy and safer than bloodletting done according to length and width."
"If syncope is likely to occur during bloodletting, you should prepare the patient beforehand with a little bread soaked in wormwood wine or simple oxymel. Remove blood at that location in three or four sessions."
"If the patient is cold in temperament, then before bloodletting, give them bread soaked in myrrh syrup or aromatic honey syrup spiced with pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and similar spices, or highly fragrant syrup."
"If syncope occurs during bloodletting due to the loss of too much blood, then you should give them water made from meat and fragrant honey syrup to drink. Use aromatics such as aloe and apply it topically around the area."
"And use the other causes that have been mentioned in the division under the chapter of syncope from evacuation."
"For those who wish to raise their arm and dissolve the blood on the second day, bloodletting should be done for excessive evacuation. The strength of the bleeding will be weak, gradually evacuating the blood according to the quantity of the strength over several days."
"However, for those who wish to raise their arm and draw blood again on the second day, and have a strong constitution, they should do so approximately 7 to 9 hours after the first bloodletting."
"But those who wish to draw blood from their body in opposition to the direction of the part that declines, it should be done on the second or third day."
"But for those bodies in which there is already scanty blood and it is sharp and causes fever, blood should be drawn from them once, drawing out a large quantity. Attention should be paid so that syncope occurs, as you will have conserved all the conditions of bloodletting. Place your hand on the pulse of their body to prevent death occurring instead of syncope, for many times this happens due to ignorance and negligence."
"And when you wish to release the arm and evacuate blood again on the second day, even if the vein opening has closed and it is difficult to draw out blood, do not press upon it with violence. Rather, press gently with the hand slightly curved, as this is too harmful."
"Let the bloodletting be done a second time until it flows freely. Or remove the acuteness of the bloodletting that has coagulated in the vein opening with a gentle pressure using tragacanth gum or saguenaria. Pause upon it and press gently until the blood flows out."
"And if the vein is inflamed, then leave it alone and do not touch it until the inflammation has subsided."
"And if there is a necessity to provoke evacuating blood again and it is not an excuse, then perform bloodletting on that location or on the other arm in another vein."
"And the vein called 'funis of the arm' is bled in place of the cephalic or basilica veins when they are not prominent or are hidden. For it consists of those."
"And the quality of bloodletting from it is that the patient places their hand in cold water until the vein becomes red and appears clearly."
"And bloodletting should be done gently with a ligature made from woolen thread with moderate tightness. And bloodletting should be performed transversely in small sections, not latitudinally nor lengthwise."
"And let the opening be wide and let your bloodletting with which you bleed that person be done just above the junction of the hand."
"And if the flow of blood is prohibited, then immerse your hand in cold water again and let the blood run into the water until your need is satisfied."
"But if it is summertime, then you are excused from immersing your hand in cold water. And the mesh is paused for bloodletting in cold water during wintertime."
"And bloodletting from this vein is safer than all other veins because it has neither a palpable vein nor nerves."
"And bloodletting of the little vein on the right hand is beneficial for diseases of the liver."
"And the quality of bloodletting from it is that you should tighten the hand with a ligature or your hand, having placed it in cold water until the vein becomes inflated and clearly visible. Perform bloodletting transversely on it; and if some of it remains, do not worry about it."
"And take care not to finish your hand during bloodletting, because there are nerves in these veins that are bare of flesh."
"And again immerse the hand in cold water and let the blood run into it, because if you do not immerse it in cold water, the blood will coagulate in the vein opening and the flow will be prohibited."
"And when blood is drawn according to the necessary quantity, then press upon the vein with oil and salt so that it does not close suddenly. And do likewise for any other wound."
"But the benefit of bloodletting from this vein on the left hand is that it is beneficial for diseases of the spleen."
"And do likewise in bloodletting this one as you did the other."
"And the benefit of bloodletting from the vein called 'sephena' is for diseases that are in the parts below the body, such as diseases of the womb, and retention of menses, and diseases of the sinews, ulcers of the skin and old sores, and their like."
"And the quality of bloodletting from it is that the patient should place their foot in cold water and make friction over it until the veins become clearly visible. Then tie a ligature around the junction of the foot; the location of the vein appears just below the said knee, and it branches out into many small branches on the face of the foot."
"And then bleed the thickest branch or one of those below the knee towards the ankle joint because it is better and safer."
"And if you bleed this vein on the face of the foot, then beware of the nerves that are near it on the face of the foot, and pause your bloodletting with that which you use for bleeding across, as if you wished to cut it."
"And let the bloodletting be moderate."
"But if you cannot draw blood, then immerse the foot in cold water again and let the blood run into it until it is evacuated."
If the flebotomist errs in the first attempt, then try again with the flebotomy a little higher up, for the vein is swollen; and do not fear the malignant humor, but guard against damaging nerves as we have said.
Similarly do the same to the other leg.
And of the saphenous vein, the location is as we have said, behind the ankle joint below the head of the fibula.
The benefit of bloodletting for this condition is to relieve pain in the hip when it is used to remove heat.
The characteristic of bloodletting for this condition is that the patient enters a bath, and quickly and firmly binds the vein on the inner side of the thigh above the ankle joint with a long thin bandage so that it does not become visible except through that.
And then when it appears, immediately flebotomize according to each vein that you are able to and according to the traverse, and it is better; or else incise that with an incision or cut that one with a section, for the location of this one is swollen.
And it is more common in men and less so in women. And if you find that one, and it does not appear to the touch at all, then immediately flebotomize some branch of this one, and it is that which appears on the back of the hand towards the little finger and the ring finger.
And beware of the nerves, and let flow as much blood as you wish.
And moreover untie the ligature and press on the place of the bloodletting firmly for a short time, for it heals easily.
Concerning venesection and the qualities to use that one
Bloodletting is done with a lance, or a needle, or a vein-opener.
And bloodletting is done in two ways: one of them is with scarification and extraction of blood, and the other is bloodletting without scarification.
And this bloodletting that is without scarification is done in two ways, for either it is with fire or without fire.
And the places on the body where bloodletting is administered with scarification and extraction of blood are fourteen in number, among which one is where bloodlettings are paused: at the nape of the neck, which is the last part of the head; and the middle place of it on both parts of the neck equally; and bloodlettings on the chin, below the jawbone but above the mouth; and bloodlettings on the two spatulas; and bloodlettings on the hollow of the hand, which is at the end of the wrist; and bloodlettings on the two elbows, which are on the two arms; and bloodlettings on the two knees; and bloodlettings on the two ankles.
And bloodletting does not extract blood except from the small veins scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not cut off virtue by those means, just as it is done by phlebotomy; nor is it necessary that bloodletting be done with fire or without fire in any illness caused bypletion until the whole body has been evacuated.
But if bloodletting is provoked by illness or by continuity, we administer it at any hour at the beginning of the month and at the end of it, and in the middle of it and at any time.
And therefore when there are times in any of those causes, and particularly if it is at the third or mid-month, we command bloodletting to be done after two or three hours have passed since that time.
And the benefit of bloodletting from the nape of the neck is that when it alleviates heaviness in the head and prevents collapse on the eyes, but it is necessary that this be an appropriate evacuation of the whole body.
And this bloodletting is located at the site of phlebotomy of the cephalic vein
It is not right to use this [bloodletting] in those who have a feverish condition or catarrh, for it gives great harm.
And therefore it is not necessary to use that bloodletting on the elderly, and on those whose heads have feverish illnesses
But above that, if it is continued upon it, forgetfulness occurs; and therefore you should command the bloodletter to pause his hand slightly after the bloodletting at the places where forgetfulness is generated.
But bloodletting from the armpit is located at the site of phlebotomy of the dark vein and the basilica vein: and therefore it alleviates asthma, and constriction of the breath, and the division of the windpipe of the lung, and coughing, and repletion.
And it is necessary that the armpit bloodletting be done gently, for if it is done forcefully it generates weakness in the body and stomach.
And bloodletting from the temple alleviates accidental pains in the head and ophthalmia, migraine, and pleurodynia, and toothache; and it is located at the site of phlebotomy of the basilica vein
And you should command the bloodletter not to press his hand during scarification lest he wound the artery and cause bleeding
And bloodletting below the chin alleviates hoarseness in the mouth and corruption of the gums, and it is similar to those illnesses that are in the mouth; and it stands at the site of phlebotomy of Alephairic, which are on both lips.
But bloodletting that is done over the two shoulder-blades alleviates headaches, which are caused bypletion of heat.
And bloodletting from the two places below the eyebrows alleviates the benefit of phlebotomy of three veins, that is, the basilica, dark, and cephalic veins, for it attracts blood from all those veins multiplied in the flesh, and those small veins from the other veins more thick until attraction reaches the three veins.
And command the bloodletter not to proceed with scarification, for that place is devoid of flesh, and thus it has nerves and arteries there
And it is a bloodletting with which blood is let from the buttocks and alleviates hemorrhoids of the anus and ulcers that are there
And you should command the bloodletter that it be a large bloodletting, and of iron, for that place requires strong sectioning; and many subtle bloodlettings are drawn out by strong suction, and it should be scarified with scarification
But bloodlettings from the calves diminish by diminution evidently for they draw out blood from all the body and alleviate old pains of the kidneys and abdomen, and bladder; and they provoke menstruation and alleviate botch and dimple; and they stand at the site of phlebotomy of two saphenous veins, Alachoben, and two cavillas.
But they greatly weaken the whole body and cause fainting in many men
And bloodletting at Alachoben has benefit similar to that of bloodletting from both calves
"The position of the windpipe is such that it begins wide and gradually narrows due to suction. Do not prolong this position excessively, but rather pause gently and remain quietly so that the humors can come together evenly." "And do not stop iterating this until you see the spot already reddening and swelling, and notice the appearance of blood's color."
"And then you shall slowly scratch and irritate the skin little by little, taking care with the position of the body."
"And that man who has tender skin from few hairs, it is necessary that you scratch him once and not twice, for the place not to become ulcerated."
"And command the blower to amplify the scarification, and press gently, and keep the suction easy."
"And if the blood is thickened, then it is necessary to scratch twice, for in the first time the way of subtleization in the blood and its moisture is opened." "But on the second occasion, with careful scrutiny, the extraction of thick blood should be obtained."
"And if the blood is too fetid, then the third scratch should not be done so that it can succeed."
"Finally, when we want to extract blood little by little or a little bit, one scratch is enough for us."
"And if we want to extract much blood, we scratch with much scarification; and if we know that the blood is thick, then it is necessary to scratch for a strong scarification."
"The term 'scarification' refers only to the depth of the cut."
"And if the skin of that person is thick, hard, dark, and its pores are narrow, then the places where the cups will be used should be anointed with lenitive, opening, and dissolving substances; if it is in summer, thus as oil of aloe or violet oil, or oil of bitter almonds, or oil of cumin seed; and if it is in winter, then narcissus oil, lily oil, camomile oil, or blood should be used for those similar."
"And if the superfluity is thick and fatty, then the oil should be bitter almond, balsamite oil, aloe oil, or aneth oil, and similar ones."
"But if the person being cupped has wide pores and tender skin, then it is prohibited to use oil; and for this person, the places where the cups will be applied should be washed with warm or hot water of solatrum, cumin seed water, or pennyroyal water, and similar ones to those."
"And for the person whose blood is very moist, wash his cups with sour wine, or myrtle and sumac water, and similar ones."
"And for the person whose superfluities are thick, wash his cups with old wine, or water of sansuc (majoram), or decoction of aneth, or chamomile, and similar ones."
"And it is necessary that the cupping be done before a bath; having to administer it close to the moment of bathing for one or two hours, and it is necessary that he/she sleeps close to the cupping."
"What is this: that it is necessary for the person being cupped to be regulated before cupping."
"And it is necessary to consider at the beginning: if the person being cupped or the one who should bleed him/her has a choleric nature and vents over sharp blood and inflammation, then he/she should take causes of cooling, such as sour apple milk, chicory with vinegar and lettuce, and secanolabum, julep, and similar ones."
"And pause their foods such as pheasants, birds of prey meat, and sour seasoned foods, and similar ones."
"And for the person whose complexion is cold, it is necessary that he/she drink rosehip syrup with honey, or syrup of fennel seed, sumac, and myrrh, and let him/her be advised to use sparingly of drinking and eating, and avoid foods of pheasant, rabbit, partridges, small birds, and pigeons."
"And it is necessary that on the day of cupping and bloodletting, drinking should be greater than eating."
"And it is necessary to give some men tyriaca altharca or muscatel medicaments, such as musk powder, or alcelet before cupping or bloodletting, so that the principal members are comforted and that the blood be subtilized; but those who have scabies should not take it."
"But the cupping that is not done with scarification are those that are done to pause its liver, and on the navel and gout, and on the umbilicus, in the joints of the elbows, and the armpit of the axilla, because these members do not suffer scarification upon them."
"And it is not desired for these except the attraction of blood from the member, such as pausing cupping on the breast in disease of flux of bloody blood from the nose; and they use it so that cold hard inviscid cupping may be dissolved from the member, such as pausing on the abdomen and navel; because this rarifies the member and scratches it and removes pain by resolving the cupping."
"And already cupping is paused on the temples when there occurs in them oppression or dizziness, because by virtue of strong attraction it draws out oppression and expels dizziness from its place."
"And similarly, it does when cupping is paused on the liver and spleen to resolve that which is enclosed therein."
"And these cuppings are administered with suction only; but some are also administered with fire."
"And sometimes they are administered full of warm water in the diseases of the spleen."
"And this is why the cupping should be filled and made larger, that is cold water alone or water in which suitable herbs are cooked."
"Form of cupping administered with fire: let the width of the opening be that of two fingers, according to how we have formed it; and let the quantity of the pitch be at most a palmful; and let it be on his side, in the place that is in the circuit, as much as him/her, and let the wick be small according to the quantity that enters into it like a needle."
"Let it be made of wormwood or citrus with thick margins, lion's tooth, hawthorn and myrtle, so that the member does not hurt from its position upon it."
"And let it be placed in the middle of the transverse line of wormwood or iron where the candle with fire is paused."
"And already this cupping should be much larger than that which we have recommended, and the lesser one according to the diseases and state of him/her who uses it."
"And the cuppings of children and weak ones are different from those of young people and robust ones."
"And the quality of pausing this cupping with fire on the member is that it extends the mecha with fire from decently burned wood before a small candle of wax, and pauses it on the middle of the transverse line in the middle place of the cupping, so that the fire may be kindled around the edge without burning the body of the sick person."
"And immediately it should be paused on the member of the sick person, and let the wick that we have said be on top, until when we have the cuppings and do not need to hold the wick, then the vapor will rise over that wick, immediately the cupping will be dissolved."
"And soon after, extinguish the wick according to its manner, and repeat it if necessary."
"But in cupping that is administered in the disease of pleurisy with water, there is neither transverse line nor wick, and it is not administered except that it should be filled with water, and it is paused on the member alone."
"And this is its form: And this cupping, the larger it is, the better, for it can receive a large quantity of water."
